“You don’t understand—this place isn’t what we thought it was.
I was wrong. We were so wrong.”
— E L I Z A B E T H S H AW
141G A M E
M O T H E R
S E C T I O N
The Lost Worlds is a sandbox campaign for frontier
colonists, set in the distant reaches of the Far Spin-
ward Colonies. The player characters—blue collar,
salt of the earth, hard-working types—are part of an
ambitious expedition in search of these colonies, lost
nearly a century ago. Their goal: to find them, make
the people safe, re-colonize the sector, and bring it
back into the embrace of human society.
But this campaign isn’t just a colony mission, it’s
also about exploring alien worlds. The PCs will dis-
cover the breathless wonders of the galaxy, and trade
them in for enough fat Company dollars to retire on.
T H E
The campaign consists of six expeditions to differ-
ent Far Spinward Colonies, which can be played in any
order, and a seventh campaign finale. There are also
rules to generate encounters at any of the other colo-
nies too. As your PCs travel, they will learn clues about
the terrible threats playing out across this space,
leading them to the single-minded bio-mechanical
organisms known as the Perfected, and their intent to
remake humankind in their dreadful image. They will
reach the final climactic expedition where they must
face this terror and decide the destiny of all.
F A R S P I N W A R D
C O L O N I E S
SETTLE DOWN FOR A HISTORY LESSON
By the 2050s the unfettered growth of the mega-cor-
porations meant that private equity led the way to
the stars. The British Weyland Corporation estab-
lished settlements in what became known as the Far
Spinward Colonies, then brought them under the aus-
pices of the newly formed Three World Empire. But
while Weyland and the 3WE were the prime movers
behind this expansion, the colonists themselves
came from all walks of life, including the Chinese
Asian Nations Cooperative (CANC), a supernation
subsequently absorbed by the UPP. All told, eighteen
colonies were established, inhabited by millions of
hopeful pioneers.
Then, 75 years ago—disaster. The space between
the Outer Rim and the Far Spinward Colonies was
scoured by massive solar ejections, gamma bursts
and waves of radiation. The time known as “the Isola-
tion” had come. Travel was made impossible, and all
communication with the new colonies was lost. Cut off
from the Middle Heavens, the Far Spinward Colonies
were left to fend for themselves and forgotten.
Until now. Looking for a common cause to unite
the squabbling superpowers, the United Nations pro-
posed a multi-national expedition, the Great Mother
Mission, to unite humanity behind a common goal and
reclaim the lost colonies.
FA S T F O R WA R D T O 2 1 8 5
Those 75 years have been tough for the citizens of the Far
Spinward Colonies. The radiation storms wreaked havoc,
and the loss of their supply lines from home was a terrible
blow. Some colonies managed to hold on, re-focusing their
efforts on just staying alive. Others fell into barbarism and
infighting. Some failed completely, leaving no survivors.
On top of all that, the colonists disturbed something
that had long been asleep. The Fulfremmen, aka the
14 2
Perfected, had been hibernating, waiting to be found by
living, breathing creatures so they could continue their
one mission in life: to infect—to make perfect—everything
they find. Three colonies quickly fell to them, before the
settlers could mount a resistance. Some fell back to hide
in their colonies or hold the line there. Others took more
direct action, to try and keep the Perfected at bay.9 .
T H E
L O S T
W O R L D S
THE FULFREMMEN
The Fulfremmen are relentless in pursuit of two objec-
tives—their need to spread their “perfection” to every
living and mechanical entity they can, and their desire
to cultivate an Empress hive of XX121 Xenomorphs, a
“hive of hives,” as a sacred monument to the majesty
of these creatures.
The Perfected were created by an advanced
humanoid species known as the Engineers—Homo
Gentior—who, in their attempts to recreate an ancient
alien lifeform they called the Destroying Angel, also
created humankind, the Arcturians and the Proto-
morph. Despite their technological mastery the
Engineers came into conflict with their creations—the
Perfected persisted, the Engineers did not.
S I T U AT I O N : Asleep for millennia, the Perfected
were accidentally awoken after the Far Spinward Col-
onies were isolated from the Middle Heavens. Capelli,
Kareti and July Colonies were overrun and transformed
into Proto-Hives (page 129). Sanchez Colony was
destroyed before they could transform it. But the Per-
fected’s ability to spread has been hampered by a lack
of both navigational data for the Middle Heavens and
spaceships with FTL drives that can cover the distance.
One year ago, a congregation of the Children of
the Two Divines traveled to the Far Spinward Colonies
and found them. The Perfected gave some the gift of
perfection, but immediately saw the value in keeping
others un-perfected, to use as moles within the col-
onies, to infiltrate them and search for a ship to help
them fulfill their destiny.
The Children of the Two Divines also brought a gift:
an offering of XX121 eggs. The Perfected have been
cultivating xenomorph hives ever since and nurturing
an Empress to rule over them all. The Perfected know
of the Engineer relic they call the “Lychgate” and
see this as the perfect place to establish this “hive
of hives.”
P L AY I N G T H E P E R F E C T E D : The Perfected are
above all motivated to spread their infection. They are
relentlessly seeking navigation data for the Middle
Heavens, and ships that can cover the 30 parsecs to
their destination (see the expeditions Against a Sea of
Troubles and Let Sleeping Gods Lie, and the campaign
event Wolf in Sheep’s Clothing on page 169). As the
campaign develops, they become aware of the Great
Mother Mission, and will use the lure of the Engineer
Lychgate as a honeypot, to draw the colony ship
UNCSS Ìyánlá to them, so they can capture it as a prize
beyond their wildest dreams (see the expedition “In
the Shadow of Perfection”).
THE CHILDREN OF THE TWO DIVINES
The Children of the Two Divines are all servants to the
Perfected, and they work to further the Perfected’s
ambitions at all times.
S I T U AT I O N : Under the leadership of a rogue
android, Mother Ma’Kayla, this extremist offshoot of
the Church of the Immaculate Incubation (page 164 in
the core rulebook) is nothing more than a starfaring
death cult. In 2185 they gathered Engineer star chart
data, stole a fleet of modified Heliades-class ships,
and headed for what their translations called “Perfect
Space.” Expecting to find a paradise, they instead
found the Far Spinward Colonies. Now, their leaders
have found perfection as bio-mechanoids, and their
fanatical followers raid colonies to spread the word.
Six of their Heliades-class vessels are still opera-
tional, but they suffer from a lack of spare parts and
poor maintenance. None has an FTL drive that is
capable of anything more than a short haul among
the Far Spinward Colonies, and their FTL rating is
reduced to 20.
P L AY I N G T H E C H I L D R E N : The Children of the
Two Divines are fully committed to the objectives
of the Perfected, while individual members work to
prove their worth and be elevated to the ranks of the
perfected. In the campaign finale (In the Shadow of
Perfection) they will fight to capture the UNCSS Ìyánlá.
T H E S C H I S M I N T H E D E AT H C U LT : Not all the
Children of the Two Divines have proven devoted to
the cause of perfection. Six months ago, a group led
by Chikondi Okafor realized the error of their ways
and the danger they were in. Taking one of the Heli-
ades ships they made a run for it, reaching KOI-784
and Dylan Colony on their failing fumes of fuel, before
crashing in the jungle. Rescued by the colonists, they
were soon recognized for what they were, or had been
(see the expedition To Go My Own Dark Way).
143G A M E
M O T H E R
S E C T I O N
M OTH ER MA’KAYLA
HYPERDYNE SERIES 120A/3 SYNTHETIC & STAGE
II BIOMECHANOID ABOMINATION
Single-minded and guarded, but curious, Mother
Ma’Kayla led the Children to Perfected Space, where
she was infected with a variant strain of 26 Draconis
and has now developed into a Stage II Abomination
(page 123)—unlike most strains of the black patho-
gen, this variant affects synthetics as well as humans.
She is a willing agent of the Fulfremmen and is on her
way to enlightened perfection—her skull has subtly
extended, and her arms and legs have increased in
bulk and length. However, she still retains mental
control and her love of ancient Earth poetry.
STRENGTH 7, AGILITY 7, WITS 6, EMPATHY 1

HEALTH: 7
SKILLS: Mobility 2, Ranged Combat 3, Observation 2
A NOTE FROM MU/TH/UR: As a Mutated Abomination (page 123), Ma’ Kayla
cannot use EMPATHY-based skills, firearms, or other technological
items, and is immune to MANIPULATION. She suffers damage as an
android. ■
GORHAM’S MARAUDERS
14 4
Gorham’s Marauders prowl the Far Spinward Colonies,
seemingly little more than pirates preying on the weak.
However, they have only one purpose—to prevent the
Perfected from leaving this sector of space. But first
things first. To do that they must survive.the core rulebook), blockading Perfected Proto-Hive
planets and destroying any Perfected vessels they find.
They have also been raiding colonies, to systematically
purge navigation charts, denying the Perfected the
knowledge to track humanity back to Earth.
T H E S I T U AT I O N : Gorham’s Marauders are colo-
nists who took it upon themselves to keep the Per-
fected from spreading across space. On his deathbed,
the original pioneer J.V. Gorham inspired his people to
destroy Sanchez Outpost before the Perfected could
transform it, leaving it a nuclear wasteland. Since
then, they have operated out of the ruined Seegson
platform orbiting Sanchez Colony, Finland Station
(the same design as Novgorod Station, page 358 ofP L AY I N G T H E M A R A U D E R S : The PCs will
encounter Gorham’s Marauders during the expedition
Let Sleeping Gods Lie and may come across them in
space (see the campaign event Gorham’s Marauders).
But if the PCs can build a relationship with them, they
can be called upon to help defend the UNCSS Ìyánlá
and finally defeat the Perfected (see the expedition In
the Shadow of Perfection).9 .

CAPTAIN J.V. GO R HAM III
Jovial, light-hearted but committed to her task, she is
the great granddaughter of the legendary J.V. Gorham.
At 22 years old, the pirate leader has the legacy of her
family to live up to. Her grandfather and father were
responsible for taking the fight to the Perfected.

T H E C O O P E R AT I V E
WAR LO RD ZH A
ˉ N GJIÉ
The Cooperative, under Colonel-turned-Warlord
Zhāngjié, has ambitions to dominate this region
of space, and will always try to turn any situation
to their advantage.
T H E S I T U AT I O N : The Cooperative is the
last bastion of the now defunct Chinese Asian
Nations Collective (CANC). They were forced to
abandon the failing Curzic Outpost after the Iso-
lation, finding refuge on May Outpost, a former
Three World Empire royal marine base. However,
after years of squabbling, the CANC finally used
force to subjugate the remaining marines and
take over. The Cooperative has thrived—in a
fashion—under Warlord Zhāngjié’s iron-fisted
leadership. Enhancing their own society through
press-ganging people from other colonies, they
restored the industry on May Outpost, and have
protected their people from invading forces.
A I R P O W E R : The Cooperative has two oper-
ational Bison CM-88B Freighters with four drop
shuttles each. They use these to raid other colo-
nies and take what they need from these worlds
(stats as per the Bison G on page 181 of the core
rulebook but equipped with a Short Lance ASAT
missile launcher and two Tactical Nukes each).
Long ago they had their long-range nav data
wiped, and the Cooperative tend to steer well
clear of Gorham’s Marauders, given half a chance.
Power-hungry, violent but logical. While Zhāngjié’s
philosophy is “might is right” he tries to rule benev-
olently. However, if his authority is challenged, he
will respond with furious anger. Zhāngjié believes
the Engineer pyramid on May Outpost holds a secret
that will secure his future as a conquering hero, if he
can find a way to explore it safely (see the expedi-
tion The Devil Lives In Still Waters).

USCSS COVENANT
TIME FOR ANOTHER
HISTORY LESSON
In 2180, the United Nations proposed that a
multi-national, multi-corporation expedition
should travel to learn the fate of the Far Spin-
ward Colonies and reconnect them to the Middle
Heavens. Recession, and the recollection of
the abundance in the old colonies, made this
a mouth-watering prospect to the UA, 3WE,
and UPP alike—the Great Mother Mission was
established by the United Nations Interstellar
Settlement Corps (UNISC), under the command
of a UN bureaucrat, Governor Kholwa Abantu.
Naturally the Interstellar Commerce Commission
(ICC) were to be well-represented, to ensure fair
play and all safety protocols were stringently
followed.
A colossal Deucalion-class colony ship—the
UNCSS Ìyánlá—was launched in 2182, with its
four Magellan-class support ships: the UNCSS
Umsindisi, UNCSS Solovetsky Island, UNCSS
Chimata-no-kami, and UNCSS Typhoon. With the
addition of three Throop Rescue and Recovery
CM90V Corvus-class salvage vessels, the flotilla
was ready to sail.
14 6
U N C S S Ì YÁ N L Á
The UNCSS Ìyánlá is a Lockmart and Welsun Type
3300B Deucalion-class X modular colony carrier
(page 77), coming in at 2,550m in length,
with a beam of 450m and draft of 300m. This
state-of-the-art long-range spacecraft carries
four externally mounted Atmospheric Processor
Plant modules, four ring-mounted Magellan-­
class J Space Exploration Vehicles, as well as
numerous drop-shuttles, support craft, and
ground vehicles. Three “spines” run the length
of the vessel, with transit systems for crew and
equipment.
UNCSS ÌYÁNLÁ

for point defense against incoming

T H E
L O S T
W O R L D S
U N CSS ÌYÁN LÁ
COMMAND MODULE
Houses all flight controls, including the bridge and communications, all com-
mand and mission administration functions and briefing rooms. The senior
officers and flight crew live here.
TRANSIT MODULE
Contains air locks, hangar bays, ready rooms, and tactical ops centers.
Revived colonists are housed here before transit off-ship. There are six
docking arms, and the mission’s four SEVs dock to this module.
CRYOSLEEP MODULES A-D
Each module contains 2,500 colonists in cryosleep, with rehabilitation and
re-orientation facilities.
ENGINEERING AND
ATMOSPHERE PROCESSORS
The engineering section manages the maintenance of the
ship and its systems and includes a manufactory module for
building vehicles and equipment. It also houses the maga-
zine for Ìyánlá’s supply of terraforming tactical nukes, and
hangars for supply and repair vessels. All colony equipment
is shipped in bulk from here. This module also contains
extensive quarantine facilities. There are four externally
mounted Atmosphere Processor units attached to this
module—fully automated, they can be deployed to any
area of clear ground (1000m square) and will automatically
begin set-up and operations.
CRYOPRESERVATION AND STORE MODULES 1–4
Contains all the stores and equipment to support colonization operations,
including all cryopreserved human embryos and livestock.
100×100
METERS
DRIVE MODULE
Contains engines, reactors, fuel stores, the solar sail arrays, and recharge
facilities, as well as all the machinery and equipment required to make the
ship fly.

W E Y L A N D -Y U TA N I
The senior W-Y corporate on board is Director
Kamal Vartouhi, but day to day running of Wey-
land-Yutani’s affairs, and the colony ship UNCSS
Ìyánlá, are overseen by a Platinum Edition reissue
of the Walter series synthetic, called Gaius.
Most of the Far Spinward Colonies were
established by the old Weyland Corporation and
had fallen under the authority of the 3WE before
the Isolation. Director Vartouhi naturally wants
to see these outposts returned to the fold and
ensure that Weyland Corporation’s centuries-old
investment finally pays off but is less concerned
by this than the 3WE seems to be.
Vartouhi is even more interested in the other
treasures that the Far Spinward Colonies may
offer. The corporation’s generosity—contrib-
uting the MU/TH/UR 9000 mainframe for the
UNCSS Ìyánlá as well as donating all four of the
Magellan-class SEVs, each equipped with a DA/
UT/UR 2200 FTL-linked back to Ìyánlá’s MU/TH/
UR—was not done from the goodness of their
heart. Through this network they can observe
and eavesdrop on the activities of the whole
expedition and ensure they don’t miss any excit-
ing finds (see the campaign event MU/TH/UR
Knows Best).
14 8
THE MISSION
M A N DAT E
The United Nations Interstellar Settlement Corps’
Mandate for the mission derives from the articles
of the pan-national Great Mother Mission Accord
of 2181, signed by all participating nations and
agencies.
The mission parameters are as follows:
1 Establish contact with the Far Spinward Col-
onies and provide immediate humanitarian
support as necessary.
2 Survey the sector and establish new UN-ad-
ministered colonies.
3 Recover existing colonial records for each
colony, stored in local Long Data Discs.
4 Negotiate terms under which surviving colo-
nies should return to UNISC oversight.
5 Assess the future technological, industrial,
and financial potential.
6 Adhere to all Interstellar Commerce Commis-
sion protocols and regulations and collabo-
rate in the spirit of the greater good.
“GREAT PARTNERSHIP”
On the eve of launch, the Secretary General of the
UN gave an address to the people of Earth:
“We are blessed, all of us here today, to see what
humankind can do when we put our heads together
in cooperation, rather than bang our heads together
in confrontation. The Great Mother Mission has
brought about ‘the Great Partnership,’ the partner-
ship of all the supernations and mega-corporations,
working together for the good of humankind.
Together you will find the lost colonies, restore their
people, banish the isolation and bring our lost broth-
ers and sisters back into the family of humanity. The
Great Mother Mission is a beacon of collaboration
and friendship—an example to all of a better future,
standing not arms versus arms, but arm in arm!
Godspeed Ìyánlá!”9 .
UNITED AMERICAS
More than anything, the UA joined the expedition
to keep an eye on their rivals, and now enemies,
the UPP. The news of the Frontier War back home
has not immediately opened hostilities within the
Great Mother Mission, thanks to the mediation of
Governor Abantu. But tensions are simmering and
the UA leadership, under Valentina Berezi, keep
trying to provoke the UPP into doing something
stupid (see the campaign event Baiting the Bear).
T H E
L O S T
W O R L D S
COLONY RECORDS
Each settlement in the Far Spinward Colonies
was set up with a recording mechanism called a
Long Data Disc—a black box for the colony. These
recorded petabytes of data about all aspects of
the colony, as well as the Command Team logs and
reports. Usually housed within a central Command
Post, Administration office or Extrasolar Colonial
Administration center these 50cm long black cylin-
ders are fitted with a handle for easy extraction and
mobility (heavy items).
THREE WORLD EMPIRE
The 3WE is focused on two things: bringing their
former colonies back within the fold before they can
be incorporated under the UNISC and keeping a lid on
the growing support for the break-away New Albion
Protectorate (NAPRO). Under their mission leader,
Colonel David Buston, they will jealously guard their
interests as former overlords of the Far Spinward
Colonies, and seek to suppress, and eventually crush,
the NAPRO sympathizers within their ranks (see the
campaign event Bring Them to Heel).
UNION OF PROGRESSIVE PEOPLES
The UPP, always wary, long suspected that the other
nations were conspiring to exclude them from the riches
to be found amongst the Far Spinward Colonies. To
avoid that outcome their mission leader, General Nurlan
Ozolinski, has taken steps to secure the new frontier for
the UPP alone. Two cells of six Ministry of Space Security
(MSS) operatives have infiltrated the expedition’s crew,
to gather intelligence on the strengths and weaknesses
of their rivals. Additionally, they have infiltrated two pla-
toons of Space Operating Forces, 60 soldiers, currently
lying in cryosleep masquerading as colonists.
When the time is right, they will awaken these sol-
diers, and take the Great Mother Mission by force (see
the expedition In The Shadow of Perfection). But that is
not all—the UPP secretly sent scouts, from its Cosmos
Exploration Corps, in four fast ships ahead of the Great
Mother Mission, to lay the ground for the UPP takeover
(see the campaign event UPP Dead in Space and the
expeditions The Devil Lives in Still Waters and In the
Shadow of Perfection).
INTERSTELLAR COMMERCE COMMISSION
Laboring under the disdain of every space-faring
organization, the ICC sees this expedition as the per-
fect time to re-assert their authority. As such, the ICC
inspectors are under orders from their chief, Superin-
tendent Jim Busby, to get into everything being done
by the expedition—they will be especially stringent
about quarantine protocols for items or specimens
that may be of extra-terrestrial origin. They are going
to make a nuisance of themselves and be a problem
for any treasure-hungry PCs (see the campaign event
Quarantine is Not a Dirty Word).
149G A M E
M O T H E R
S E C T I O N
G EN ERAL N U R LAN OZO LIN S KI
THROOP RESCUE
AND RECOVERY
Austere and haughty, but compassionate, Ozo-
linski is a career UPP soldier, having risen from the
enlisted ranks to high command. He knows that
conflict is a necessary evil, but regrets that young
lives must be shattered through it—he witnessed
much death and suffering as a young SOF soldier.
He wishes that the Great Mother Mission could
have progressed as a collaboration, but this will
not stop him giving the order to take control
(see the expedition In the Shadow of Perfection).
However, if the PCs can convince him of the threat
presented by the Perfected (with an opposed
MANIPULATION test) he will order his men to
defend the UNCSS Ìyánlá first, before resolving
the political infighting of the mission itself.
STRENGTH 5, AGILITY 3, WITS 3, EMPATHY 4
HEALTH: 5
SKILLS: Close Combat 2, Mobility 1, Ranged
Combat 2, Command 3, Manipulation 2,
Observation 2
Throop Rescue and Recovery is a highly
regarded private company under the leadership
of Alecto Throop. TR&R has been contracted
by the UN to provide support operations as
part of the Great Mother Mission and brings
three Corvus-class ships at the expedition’s
disposal. Throop answers to Governor Abantu.
TR&R can be called in to rescue the PCs should
they become stranded (see the campaign event
Throop to the Rescue).
Throop herself has had a long and exciting
career. Biologically in her 80s, she appears
about 50 years old. Many years ago, she had an
encounter with the XX121 Xenomorph, something
she will never forget.
THE MINOR
C O R P O R AT I O N S
Hyperdyne Corporation (under Director Pereira
Abrams), Omni-Tech Resources (CEO Kim Bak)
and the Kelland Mining Company (Prospector
General Lee Taylor) are all signed on for the
Great Mother Mission. They see this as the
chance to elevate their companies into the big
leagues and will scrabble for resource rights and
contracts as hard as anyone.
TALENT: Field Commander, Influence
GEAR: Covert body armor (Armor Rating 3),
MP-4043 Grach pistol.
THROOP’S NIGHTMARES
The PCs can learn much about the Xenomorphs from
Throop, should they seek her help once they have come
face to face with the space beast. They will need to
build a positive relationship with her, but once she hears
they have encountered the beast she will offer guidance,
at your discretion. She will finish by saying: “It is elegant,
fast and terrible. It exists to destroy and destroys to
exist. Once seen it will never be forgotten...”
15 0
THE NEW ALBION
P R O T E C T O R AT E
Not officially represented on the Great Mother
Mission, there are several members of the 3WE
who openly sympathize with the New Albion
Protectorate’s position. Led by the senior 3WE
administrator Lynna Young-Hee, this faction
gathers support as the campaign progresses,
until the 3WE decides to put a stop to it with
force (see the campaign event Bring Them to
Heel). ■9 .
T H E
L O S T
W O R L D S
R U N N I N G T H E L O S T
W O R L D S C A M P A I G N
The campaign consists of seven scenarios—six expe-
ditions, playable in any order, and a climactic finale.
Outside of these, we are introducing a new concept
to this campaign: campaign events. Just like events
in a Cinematic scenario, campaign events provide
extra scenes and challenges for the PCs that can be
placed into the campaign whenever you like, binding
the overall story together and providing an exciting
countdown to the finale.
T H E M E TA P U Z Z L E : The campaign also presents
a Metapuzzle for the PCs to unravel. Each expedition
(and some campaign events) offers the PCs the chance
to find clues to that Metapuzzle which, by the end of
the sixth expedition, will reveal the terrible truth of the
Perfected’s plans—what the PCs do with that knowledge
is up to them. Read more about the Metapuzzle on
page 161. ■

to further explore, or even colonize, them. The
this campaign offers, you should allow your play-
rules here, and in the Appendix: Building Your

Own Better World, will help you create those
course through it. If you are comfortable creating
adventures, and the planets and new colonies that

RUMORS, HEARSAY AND GOSSIP
Aside from the Metapuzzle clues, there is other
information the PCs can learn from almost any col-
onist NPC. You should feel free to give out these
details if the PCs have earned the information
from an NPC or other source:
TSince the Isolation, the colonies have fallen
apart. There has been little cross-colony com-
munication in decades.
TSome have chosen piracy, preying on the already
weakened colonies.
T
An organization known as the Cooperative is the
worst for raiding, kidnapping people and killing
those who resist.
TAll told, many hundreds of thousands must
have died.
TThe people of the Far Spinward Colonies are
angry with Weyland Corp and the 3WE, as they
feel they were deserted and left to rot.
TSome colonies have fallen to some kind of pesti-
lence that spread to more than one planet.
T
Some say that this pestilence is even worse, that
someone out there is actively spreading it.
TThere were rumors of new ships in the sector last
year, not from the colonies but from the Middle
Heavens.
151G A M E
M O T H E R
S E C T I O N
T H E P L A Y E R
C H A R A C T E R S
In The Lost Worlds, the player characters are employ-
ees or contractors working on the Great Mother Mis-
sion. They have a job to do, but will be able to choose
where they go, what they do, and how they do it. They
will find the shattered fragments of former colonies,
brave new worlds to explore and exploit, the remnants
of an ancient civilization and the menace that threat-
ens the safety of every human alive.
T H E P C S ’ R O L E : The PCs are all members of the
same crew, serving on the UNCSS Solovetsky Island,
one of the mission’s four Magellan-class J Science
Exploration Vessels (SEV). While the ship has an NPC
crew that covers the basic roles needed on board, the
PCs can play any role on the vessel they please. Also,
the game is at its most “sandboxy” if one PC is the
ship’s commander.
P C A F F I L I AT I O N : Each PC will either be affiliated
to a supernation or mega corporation, or be an inde-
pendent contractor hired by the UNISC. Either choose
or roll on the table below to find out. Don’t worry if
you don’t like the outcome—your PC may be affiliated
in a certain way, but it brings great roleplaying oppor-
tunities if they don’t like it!
C O N N E C T I O N T O T H E M I S S I O N : Do the PCs
have any connection to the Great Mother Mission other
than the hunt for a great pay day? They will have their
own Personal Agendas and may be die-hard supporters
of one supernation or corporation. But this is about
their connection to the mission itself. Roll on the table
on the next page, or feel free to choose an option that
is consistent with the PC’s agenda and back story:
T H E P C S ’ R E S P O N S I B I L I T I E S : As a member
of the Great Mother Mission, the PCs are paid to play
their part in that mission. They have a contract (on
page 172) and need to follow it.
E A R N I N G A L I V I N G : In the multi-faceted
conglomeration that is the Great Mother Mission,
differences in currencies and payment traditions
would have baked-in unfair practices and inequality
of reward. So, the UNISC adopted the Weyland-Yutani
dollar as the mission’s currency. Weekly pay for your
PCs, based on their roles within the mission, can be
found on page 162 of the core rulebook. Time in cryos-
leep is paid at a rate of one-quarter of the employee’s
salary per week.
Taking account of the months in cryosleep this may
feel like a lot, but it’s small beer for being away from
family and friends for years on end and facing the dan-
gers of deep space. The real money is made in bonuses
earned for finds, resource claims and extra-curricular
activities not covered in your basic contract.

1None—you’re in this for the money.
2You are curious about what happened out in the Far Spinward Colonies, but beyond that this is just a
job to you.
3The people of the colonies must be suffering. The Great Mother Mission is vital in helping them recover.

see which one. You need to find their descendants, or find out what happened to them, if you can.

while you work to find that new future.
6You’re all-in for a new life and future. Your entire family and many friends are in cryosleep on UNCSS Ìyánlá
waiting for you to find them their new home.
UNCSS SOLOVETSKY ISLAND
MANUFACTURER: WELAND YUTANIFTL RATING: 10ARMAMENTS: As an SEV the
CREW: 6–18SIGNATURE: +0AI: DA/UT/UR 2200THRUSTERS: +8LENGTH: 150 mHULL: 6Solovetsky Island only possesses
defensive capabilities. It has two
Sensor Drone hardpoints and
three Sensor Decoys (page 177
of the core rulebook)
ARMOR
RATING: 6
UNCSS SOLOVETSKY ISLAND
The UNCSS Solovetsky Island is one of four identical
vessels on the Great Mother Mission, along with the
UNCSS Umsindisi, Chimata-no-kami, and Typhoon.
It is a Magellan-class J SEV, with a crew of up to
16 and an FTL Rating of 10. It’s equipped with two
Class D Lifeboats, one configured as a science facility,
the other as a relief boat, along with 12 Class A EEV
pods. It carries four Daihotai series 8×8 Tractors, four
Alphatech XT-37C 4×4 off-road vehicles, two EVA-7C
salvage and rescue pods and two heavy excavators. It
has cryosleep beds for 18 people, and MedPods for 12
seriously injured patients.
The UNCSS Solovetsky Island can carry up to 100
for short journeys or in an emergency. The cargo hold
is full of humanitarian essentials with spare parts and
tools for any everyday problem. The crew is cross-
trained in multiple disciplines, but would usually
consist of the commander, two pilot-navigators, two
mechanics, two security officers, one scientist, one
prospector and the ICC Protocol Inspector. In addition
to the crew, the ship is equipped with two Working
Joe androids, dubbed James and Miss Sophie by
the crew.
The crew of the Solovetsky Island, as well as those
of all other Great Mother Mission Science Exploration
Vessels, are fitted with Personal Data Transmitters
(PDTs, page 132 of the core rulebook) that can be
detected at a distance of 20 km.
T H E P C S ’ C R E W : The PCs’ crew forms a vital part
of the campaign, as they will be along for the ride.
Some will be antagonists, distrustful of the PCs and
seeking to out-maneuver them at every turn. Others
will become friends and help the PCs when they
least expect it. Some may die and will not only have
an impact on the PCs when they do, but may need
replacing with a new crew member from the UNCSS
Ìyánlá. ■

PILOT ANDI “D UDG E” D UDG EO N
He has no political axe to grind and supports the
aims of the Great Mother Mission. However, General
Ozolinski is using Dudge’s wife and child, in cryos-
leep aboard Ìyánlá
Ìyánlá,, as a lever to get Dudge to feed
useful information back to the UPP. He doesn’t want
to betray his shipmates, but his family will always
come first.
As the campaign progresses Dudge will find this
harder and harder to do, and the stress will show. If
the PCs are kind to him, he may relent and tell them
the UPP are using him as a spy. Dudge does not know
about the UPP’s plans to take control of the Great
Mother Mission.
STRENGTH 3, AGILITY 4, WITS 3, EMPATHY 3
A lover of classical pop music from the 1980s, Dudge
was run out of the Three World Empire for disobeying
orders. He joined the UPP as a mercenary, married
and made a life, becoming a naturalized UPP citizen
in 2170.

P ROS P ECTO R EMILY Q UINTANA
Quintana is an independent contractor, although she
hails from the UA city of Zihuatanejo. She distrusts
any big corporation and has little interest in politics.
Her job is to prospect and assess colonies for com-
mercial potential and development, but she just wants
to get rich and doesn’t care who she tramples to do it.
As the campaign progresses, she will keep an eye
on how the PCs behave—are they hoarding finds just
for themselves? If they are, Quintana will eventually
demand to be cut into their scam or she will report
them to the ICC authorities.

C R E W:
S ECU RITY HAMIDAH AMIR
Amir was a Royal Marine before joining the expedition.
Resourceful and strong-willed, she is disgusted that
the New Albion Protectorate has had the audacity
to break away from the 3WE. She hasn’t confronted
Monroe on her views, for the good of the crew and the
expedition, but she’s had to bite her tongue.
As the campaign progresses, she can’t wait to get
home and put the NAPRO back in its box, at the point
of her rifle. With Lakota Monroe getting increasingly
vocal in support of the NAPRO, Amir gets angrier. She
will use force to make Monroe shut her mouth.

E X P L O R I N G T H E F A R
S P I N W A R D C O L O N I E S
A total of 18 star systems were colonized before the
Isolation. Four are featured with detailed expeditions
written for them that will develop the PCs’ under-
standing of the Metapuzzle (see page 161). However,
there are another 14 previously colonized worlds that
the PCs could visit as part of the wider campaign, two
expeditions where they will have the opportunity to
colonize new worlds, and the PCs may wish to seek
out entirely new planets for colonies to start afresh
(using the rules in the Appendix: Building Your Own
Better World on page 275).

M E T A P U Z Z L E
The six clues to the Metapuzzle will ultimately allow
the PCs to reach the following understanding:
The Perfected spread an infection that wipes out life
as the PCs know it, and they are intent on spreading it
across the galaxy. But they need ships robust enough
to travel the 30-parsec distance to the Middle Heavens,
and the navigational data to make the journey—they
are actively searching for both. However, the Perfected
also believe that an Engineer relic, called “the Lych-
gate,” will allow them to instantly make the crossing.
This gate can be found in orbit around a super gas giant,
called Ojo, in the KOI-1938 system.
161G A M E
M O T H E R
S E C T I O N
But there is a twist—the Perfected know full-well they
cannot operate the Lychgate, but it’s a technological
prize of such value they reason the humans will flock
to it once they know it exists. The Perfected will use
the Lychgate as a honey trap, to lure Ìyánlá to them so
they can capture it and all its bounty.
Each clue is listed here with details on where the
PCs can find it, and handouts are provided for your
players (page 172). As the campaign is a sandbox
and the expeditions can be played in any order, some
care is needed to ensure the clues build the Metapuzzle
picture at the right pace. The key clue is #5, which
gives the PCs the spatial coordinates for the Lychgate
itself. The clue states that DA/UT/UR 2200 aboard the
Solovetsky Island is required to decode the coordinates,
so it is entirely in your power to decide when that
decoding is done, and the coordinates become avail-
able. This should happen towards the end or after you
have played the first six missions, setting the PCs up for
the race to the Lychgate and the finale.
THE SIX CLUES
# 1 D ATA B A S E R E A D - O U T F R O M H M C S S
J A N K U : Found during the expedition Home Sweet
Home, this clue explains that Gorham’s Marauders
are wiping navigation data from any ships and data-
bases they can find and trying to stop the Perfected
from spreading across space. The PCs should come
to understand that there is a threat within the Far
Spinward colonies that is seeking navigation data and
wants to reach the Middle Heavens.
# 2 M O T H E R M A’ K AY L A’ S C R U M P L E D
L E T T E R : Found during the expedition To Go My
Own Dark Way, this clue explains that the Children of
the Two Divines are looking for ship parts and naviga-
tion data, are actively helping the Perfected, and have
brought them some “gifts’’ (XX121 Ovomorphs) from
the Middle Heavens. The PCs learn about the Children
of the Two Divines, that they answer to someone or
something they revere, and some information on the
history of the Engineers and Xenomorphs taken from
the journal of the Grand Seer, Jannes Ruedi.
# 3 T H E E N G I N E E R H O L O - G LY P H S I N T H E
E N G I N E E R C I T Y : This clue is found during the
expedition Leave All Else to The Gods, and hints that
the Engineers created the Xenomorphs and the Per-
fected. Realizing they could not control their creations,
16 2
the Engineers fled this sector of space using a device
they called the Lychgate.
# 4 T H E E N G I N E E R H I E R O G LY P H I N T H E
P Y R A M I D : Found during the expedition The Devil
Lives In Still Waters, this clue reveals that the Lych-
gate exists, and is some kind of gigantic Engineer
relic that allows for instantaneous travel to anywhere
in the universe.
# 5 I N T E R P R E TAT I O N O F T H E H O L O G R A M
O R R E RY A B OA R D T H E E N G I N E E R J U G G E R -
N A U T : Found during the expedition Against A Sea
Of Troubles, this clue gives the coded coordinates for
the Lychgate, and shows it orbits a super gas giant. It
makes it clear that the Perfected intend to go there
and that the Engineers wanted to keep this artifact
from them. The PCs need DA/UT/UR 2200 to decode
the coordinates, and this may take some time.
# 6 T H E E N G I N E E R H I E R O G LY P H I N T H E
G U A R D I A N S H I P W R E C K A G E : Found during the
expedition Let Sleeping Gods Lie, this clue reveals that
the Engineers created the Perfected and the Xenom-
orphs, that the Perfected forced the Engineers to flee
from the Far Spinward Colonies region of space, and
both the Engineers and the Perfected worship or revere
the xenomorph, what they call the Destroying Angel. ■9 .

D O W N T I M E
EXPEDITION REPORTS
At the end of an expedition, the crew are expected to
file a report. In game terms, the PCs report back to the
android Gaius on UNCSS Ìyánlá (either in person or
on comms), and he assesses the bonus situation. This
should be role-played with the GM and should cover:
A debriefing of the expedition.
Recommendations for the future of the planet or
colony in question.
Requests for crew replacements, re-fuelling and
supplies / repairs.
Requests for bonuses based on:
Activities over and above the call of duty—“that
wasn’t in my contract!” (1–2 extra weeks’ salary)
The discovery of something of financial or scientific
value but without samples—“we found something
weird and pissed off, here are the co-ordinates!”
(1–3 extra weeks’ salary)
The acquisition of specimens or samples of poten-
tially valuable assets—“we found this…. Quick! Grab
T
T
T
T
T
T
T
T
it before it runs off again!” (1–10 extra weeks’ salary,
depending on the asset)
The acquisition of xenobiological or Engineer
specimens or artifacts—“if this don’t kill me, I’m
gonna buy me a planet to retire on!” (10+ weeks’
extra salary)
The PCs should justify their claims and defend against
the claims of others (PCs and NPCs) who may try to
steal their credit, and their bonuses. This may require
an opposed MANIPULATION test. However, the PCs
should always feel hard done by, and aggrieved at the
low rewards their hard work and personal risk seems
to earn.
Once this is complete the PCs should decide where
to survey next, possibly guided by the GM through the
NPC Gaius.
DOWNTIME INCIDENTS
Between expeditions there’s likely to be time to kill,
either through re-supplies and repairs, or time travel-
ing to the next expedition. Aside from spending their
hard-earned XP, there are two things that can happen:
1 Each player takes center stage and narrates a
scene involving their PC, how they are using their
downtime, who they are spending it with and what
they are doing. It might be an emotional moment
(eg, checking on their husband in cryosleep on
UNCSS Ìyánlá, or bearing their all over the horrors
of the last expedition), or funny, exciting or plain
mundane. But whatever the moment is, it belongs
to that player and their PC, although the other
players should be encouraged to build and develop
the scene if they wish.
2 They can hear about how the rest of the Great
Mother Mission is faring. Roll on the table on
page 164 and fold the results into your growing
campaign. ■
163G A M EM O T H E R
S E C T I O N
D6DOWNTIME INCIDENTS
1A random (non-expedition) colony has been explored. The PCs hear the results.
2Nothing much to report—all is in good order.
3There has been unrest between different factions within the Great Mother Mission.
Either: the 3WE has been struggling with NAPRO sympathizers.
Or: members of the UA and UPP have scuffled, and one person has been hospitalized.
Or: the UNISC has tried to mediate between the antagonistic factions but only made things worse.
4There is news from home.
Either: the UA-UPP Frontier War is escalating, and hostilities are spreading.
Or: more worlds have seceded from the 3WE and joined NAPRO.
5Either: An unknown disease has been sweeping through the UNCSS Ìyánlá’s crew. It doesn’t seem serious, but
she’s been quarantined by the ICC for D6 weeks. No re-supplies or major repairs are available until the ICC
lifts the quarantine.
Or: The UNCSS Ìyánlá has suffered damage from a local neutrino burst. It’s not serious but she must stop and
undergo essential repairs for the next 6D6 days.
6A maintenance failure on the UNCSS Ìyánlá and D6 × 100 sleeping colonists die. You decide if any of these are
connected with the PCs, or if there was foul play behind the malfunction.
S E S S I O N
“Session Zero” is the thrilling start to the campaign.
Your players should create their PCs together and
decide what roles each will play aboard their ship, the
UNCSS Solovetsky Island. They will discover their polit-
ical affiliations, family connections and learn of their
NPC crewmates. They should be given Mission Contract
WHAT’S THE STORY MOTHER?
Your Magellan SEV docks gently with the UNCSS
Ìyánlá, secured to its docking ring alongside the
three other SEVs—the Umsindisi, Chimata-no-kami
and Typhoon. As clamps thunder quietly shut, you
send a cheerful farewell message to Ìyánlá’s cap-
tain, Tadesse Kondwani. “See you in two years!”
comes the reply from the ship’s android, Gaius,
before you head to the cryo deck. Your ship’s DA/
UT/UR flickers her lights, and your canopy starts
to close. The last thing you see is the distorted
image of your ship’s Working Joes—James and
Miss Sophie, as you call them—and the last thing
you hear is one of them whisper: “sleep well.”
102 weeks and 5 days later, and thousands of
W-Y dollars banked already—this is the way to make
a living! Well, you think that until hyper-sickness

Z E R O
and Colony Status handouts (page 172), giving them
information on the Great Mother Mission and the eigh-
teen colonies the mission is going to re-discover.
Once your players have had the time to ready them-
selves and ask any questions about the mission and
their role in it, read the following text out loud:
kicks in and for the next twenty minutes you wish
you were dead. An hour later and you’re ready for
the post-arrival briefing. You and the rest of the
crew file quietly through the airlock, board the
immense UNCSS Ìyánlá where you eventually take
a seat in the spacious mess hall, alongside your
fellow pioneers. The room buzzes with conversa-
tion, one hundred voices all talking about the same
things: Have we arrived? What news from home?
This coffee is still shit.
Then Governor Kholwa Abantu stands at the
front, and calls for quiet:
“First, the good news. We have all arrived on
the fringes of the Far Spinward Colonies with-
out a hitch. Home is now more than 30 parsecs
behind us.”9 .
“But talking of home, here’s the bad news. The
United Americas and Union of Progressive Peoples
are at war. Fighting has broken out across the
frontier and hostilities are ongoing. Furthermore,
the world of New Albion has broken away from the
3WE and while there are no hostilities yet, some
fear it may come to blows. But the political stupid-
ities of our governments do not change the situa-
tion here. We are a United Nations expedition and
have a mission to fulfill for the good of humankind,
so leave your petty political rivalries back in the
Middle Heavens!”
“And talking of bad news. We have not picked
up any signals, as we had hoped we might. What
this says about the fates of the people out here, we
won’t know until we explore. But as a precaution,
for now we will keep two of our SEVs with Ìyánlá
and send only two—Typhoon and Solovetsky
T H E
L O S T
W O R L D S
Island—to reconnoiter the old colonies. Good luck
everyone, and please be careful out there.”
There’s a moment’s silence, then pandemonium
breaks out right before you. Valentina Berezi of
the United Americas leaps to her feet, pointing her
finger at the UPP General, Nurlan Ozolinski: “We
can never trust you UPP bastards!” Ozolinski pulls
himself to his impressive height, tense, restrained.
Others start to shout, while Colonel Buston and
Lynna Young-Hee of the 3WE try to intervene until
they fall into an argument about the New Albion
Protectorate. W-Y Director Kamal Vartouhi stands
still to one side, arms crossed, an onlooker, while
Governor Abantu waves his arms in a futile attempt
to restore peace. Alecto Throop, the freelance
search and rescue captain sitting next to you, leans
over—calm and collected—she says: “Didn’t think I’d
have to rescue people from inside the mothership!”
K I C K I N G O F F T H E C A M PA I G N
The campaign kicks off right here. If the PCs don’t
intervene the arguments will escalate, and blows will
be exchanged between lower ranked UA and UPP offi-
cers. The likes of Valentina Berezi and Nurlan Ozolinski
will control themselves, just.
At a suitable moment, the PCs will notice the
android Gaius has sidled up to them. He says: “Quite a
display, wouldn’t you say? I’m not convinced that these
missions shouldn’t be android only, if you ask me.” He
hands them a data disc: “Your assignments. I see little
point in delaying your departure any further. I’ll brief
you in detail when you’re en route.”
The disc contains details of the colonies from the
Colony Status handout, with three expedition locations
of your choice (not including the finale), highlighted
by Gaius as the PCs’ initial assignments, to be tackled
in any order they please. Once an expedition has been
completed Gaius should give them another assignment,
so the PCs have three options for as long as possi-
ble. You should feel free to add colony locations not
covered by the expeditions (using the tables on page
279 to generate a scenario for those locations) or
send your PCs on colonial survey expeditions to find
new planets to colonize (using the rules on page 275
to generate new star systems and worlds), but these
are entirely optional—you do not have to do this to
have a full and exciting frontier campaign.
EXPEDITIONS
H O M E S W E E T H O M E : Gorham Colony, KOI-
2650.01. An arid and dusty planet, a mining colony of
reportedly 1 million colonists in 2100. The PCs discover
just one settlement of only two families, but their
arrival re-ignites a deadly feud. They must prevent the
feud killing the last survivors of Gorham Colony, as the
planet itself tries to kill them all.
T O G O M Y O W N D A R K WAY : Dylan Colony,
KOI-784.01. A humid world of extreme temperatures
and tropical jungles, with extensive caverns exploited
for mining in 2100. The PCs find a society on a knife-
edge—a primitive community terrorized by feral
barbarians, refugees from the Children of the Two
Divines begging for help, and the death cult come to
demand their wayward children back.
1 65G A M E
M O T H E R
S E C T I O N
L E AV E A L L E L S E T O T H E G O D S : Sent on a
colonization expedition, the PCs find they are not the
first to arrive here. But, under orders from Governor
Abantu himself, they establish a new colony. As the
colony lays down roots the PCs make a terrible discov-
ery—the ancient ruins of an Engineer city, and the hor-
rors that await therein. They must confront the secrets
of the city, to save themselves and the new colony.
T H E D E V I L L I V E S I N S T I L L WAT E R S : May
Outpost, KOI-610.01. The PCs find a working community,
but on the verge of insurrection. Can they bring peace to
this conflicted society, prevent the UPP from taking con-
trol, and explore the secrets—and avoid the dangers—of
an ancient Engineer pyramid, revealed by an earthquake?
A G A I N S T A S E A O F T R O U B L E S : The PCs
are ordered to search for the missing ship, UNCSS
Typhoon, and find it dead in space, its crew missing
after the Perfected tried to capture it. They trace its
path back to the two moons of a gas giant, to find one
swamped by the Perfected’s living Proto-Hive. They
must explore a derelict Engineer Juggernaut and
confront the Perfected to save the Typhoon’s crew and
escape alive to raise the alarm.
L E T S L E E P I N G G O D S L I E : Pelican Colony, KOI-
947.01. Once a glorious agricultural paradise, Pelican
Colony has been swept clean by solar radiation. The
UNCSS Solovetsky Island finds a crashed ship—Gor-
ham’s Marauders—come to hunt the Perfected.
Harassed by automatons trying to protect them, the
PCs mount an expedition to an Engineer Guardian ship
and must face the horrors that lurk in the ancient vessel.
I N T H E S H A D O W O F P E R F E C T I O N : In orbit
around the planet Ojo, KOI-1938. The finale, as the
PCs follow the clues to the Metapuzzle, and find the
Engineer Lychgate. They face the Fulfremmen and
Xenomorph hives aboard the structure, as both the
UPP and the Perfected execute their plans to capture
UNCSS Ìyánlá for themselves. ■
C A M P A I G N
These campaign level events are intended to increase
the tension of your campaign, as well as signal a
countdown to the climactic last expedition, In the
Shadow of Perfection. Some can be introduced at any
time, or even played more than once, while others are
intended to be introduced as the campaign matures.
Guidance is provided in each event.
THROOP TO THE RESCUE
To be used at any time. Throop R&R will send one of
their vessels, a standard Model CM-90S Corvus (page
180 of the core rulebook, but with an FTL rating of 4),
commanded by Alecto Throop herself, to rescue the
PCs. How this plays out will depend on the PCs’ circum-
stances that require their rescue, but the rescue should
go wrong, or be hampered in some way. The GM should
decide how many days away rescue is, remembering
that the PCs will have to hold out against whatever
terrors are facing them until help arrives.
166
E V E N T S
QUARANTINE IS
NOT A DIRTY WORD
To be played at any time, but ideally when the
PCs have made a big find and want to hide it
from the ICC. The ICC have had enough with
the endemic efforts to subvert their regula-
tions and pull the wool over their eyes. The
ICC Inspector, Tan Blatchman, orders all acqui-
sitions and finds to be impounded indefinitely
and placed into quarantine, and instructs the
security team to enforce his ruling. All finds,
specimens and samples that are aboard the
PCs’ ship, or brought aboard, will be thor-
oughly double-checked, and any that might
contravene ICC quarantine rules (such as
Xenomorph samples or eggs, or any Engineer
tech) will be seized. The security officer on
board, Hamidah Amir, is torn—she supports
the ICC, but also sees the prospects for extra
bonuses. How will the PCs try to convince
Blatchman or Amir to turn a blind eye to their
misdemeanors?9 .
T H E
L O S T
W O R L D S
MU/TH/UR KNOWS BEST
To be played at any time. Weyland-Yutani, in the form
of Gaius and MU/TH/UR 9000, suspect that the PCs
are not telling them the truth about the treasures they
have discovered. They put pressure on the PCs to
supply their finds only to W-Y, and hint that if this was
done without the oversight of the ICC or knowledge
of the other factions, the PCs would be very well
rewarded indeed. If the PCs decline, or agree but
have no intention of following through, MU/TH/UR
takes control of the ship’s Working Joe androids,
and uses them to covertly search for, and remove,
any exciting finds without the PCs’ knowledge (with
MU/TH/UR’s oversight, the Working Joes have OBSER-
VATION 7, COMTECH 6 and MOBILITY 5). When the PCs
next check they may find their exciting discoveries
are gone.
BAITING THE BEAR
To be played at any time. The PCs hear of unrest on
the UNCSS Ìyánlá, with elements of the UA contingent
skirmishing with UPP loyalists. It hasn’t blown up into
fighting yet, but it’s a powder keg and people are play-
ing with fire. On the PCs’ ship, the 3WE ship’s counselor
and negotiator, Monroe starts gently baiting Koblenz,
the UPP mechanic and any PCs who are UPP-affiliated.
If the PCs do nothing, this will turn into a fight, with
Koblenz throwing the first punch after Monroe’s prov-
ocation. Depending on how the PCs resolve this, either
one or both Monroe and Koblenz will hold grudges
against them, for favoring the other in the dispute.
N O T S O S TAT E - O F -T H E - A R T
To be played at any time. The SEVs so generously pro-
vided by Weyland-Yutani aren’t as super as everyone
was led to believe—cutting corners and saving costs
in construction means they all suffer from relentless
mechanical glitches and failures. Whenever you wish,
roll on the Minor Component Damage table on page
198 of the core rulebook, and the UNCSS Solovetsky
Island suffers yet another breakdown. The repair takes
one Shift to complete, but if the roll is failed, the PCs
cannot make the repair until they dock with the facili-
ties on the UNCSS Ìyánlá.
C O O P E R AT I V E R A I D E R S
To be played at any time. A Cooperative raiding party
(one Heliades-class ship with two drop shuttles, each
with eight soldiers) appears on the horizon and
proceeds to land near the PCs. They are on a snatch
and grab raid, looking for skilled people they can take
home and put to work. If the PCs have completed the
expedition The Devil Lives in Still Waters, they will
have dealt with the Cooperative before, and this event
will play out depending on whether the Cooperative
are friends or enemies. Otherwise, this will be the first
time they come across the Cooperative—the soldiers
will be wary of the PCs, as they are obviously well-
equipped with advanced technology, but will still look
to kidnap some locals (or even the PCs).

power, its side door has been blown off and it’s in a
slow roll. Three Proto-Hive Nodes, fleshy man-sized
blobs, are on board, in Tactical, the Galley, and Mainte-
nance. They are slowly converting the vessel into a tiny
Proto-Hive. If the PCs board and investigate they can
learn the following:

FAC I N G T H E M A R A U D E R S
Should be played mid-campaign. The PCs detect a
ship on their scanners. It is a Gorham’s Marauders’
Corvus Model CM-90S, with ten crew and armed with
one Long Lance ASAT missile, four Short Lance ASATs
and a Medium Railgun Turret. They intend to wipe
the PCs’ navigation data. Hailed by J.V. Gorham, she
orders them to stand-to and prepare to be boarded. If
the PCs cooperate, the Marauders will be firm but not
violent. They will proceed to board and wipe the ves-
sel’s navigation data, re-installing enough for them to
navigate the Far Spinward Colonies. If the PCs resist,
the pirates will use enough force to convince them to
surrender. If they run, the pirates will use their ship’s
weapons in an attempt to disable them. If the PCs try
talking to Gorham, they may make an opposed MANIP-
ULATION test to get Gorham to respond. If they suc-
ceed, they can learn the details of the first campaign
clue (page 162), or have those details confirmed, if
they have already found it. If the PCs have completed
the expedition Let Sleeping Gods Lie they may have
met J.V. Gorham before, and this event will play out
depending on the relationship the PCs built with her.
WOLF IN SHEEP’S CLOTHING
Should be played mid-campaign. The PCs detect
another vessel, a Heliades-class (page 74).
Unknown to them, it’s the Children of the Two Divines
who have detected their ship and want to capture it
for themselves. The devotees send a distress signal,
calling for medical and humanitarian aid, claiming they
have been drifting for days since their engines failed
(a scan with a successful COMTECH roll will reveal
that the Heliades’ engines are warm, and have been
recently operational). If asked, they will claim to be
from Sanchez Colony, not realizing that the PCs may
know that Sanchez was destroyed years ago. If the
PCs dock, the Children will simply rush the airlock as
soon as it opens, gaining surprise unless the players
specifically state they are being cautious. Eight of the
crew of twelve will rush aboard, to capture it, but at
the least download navigation data from the bridge
before fleeing. If the PCs try to intercept any commu-
nications from the devotees’ ship, they will succeed
with a COMTECH roll. They will hear a short exchange.
O U T G O I N G M E S S A G E : “Intact vessel identified.
We are moving to intercept. We will continue the task
to locate the navigation data, the parts and fuel that
you need for your fleet, but if the Angels are willing,
we will bring you this vessel. Your odyssey across the
Isolation’s Gap to the Outer Rim can start immediately,
and the rest can follow soon after. Before long, the
whole Middle Heavens will be open to you.”
I N C O M I N G : “Acceptance. Hasten.”
BRING THEM TO HEEL
To be played late in the campaign, but before the
finale In the Shadow Of Perfection. The 3WE, angry at
the growing support for the NAPRO, seizes all sympa-
thizers in a coordinated operation. The commander of
the UNCSS Solovetsky Island receives a message from
Colonel Buston that all NAPRO sympathizers are to
be arrested immediately (this includes Lakota Monroe
and PC sympathizers), a command that has tacit
support from the UNISC in a desperate attempt to
keep the Great Mother Mission together. It’s up to the
commander and the PCs how this confrontation plays
out on Solovetsky Island. ■

E X P E D I T I O N S
“Come my friends, ‘tis not too late to seek a newer world […]
for my purpose holds to sail beyond the sunset.”
— U LY S S E S
175P L A Y E R
S E C T I O N
1 . H O M E
S W E E T H O M E
“An eye for an eye will only make the whole world blind.”
— M A H AT M A G A N D H I
The PCs head to Gorham Colony, KOI-2650.01, a
mining outpost on a deserted, dusty, wind-swept
planet. They find only one occupied settlement,
a ragged mining facility with just eight survivors.
Their arrival re-ignites a feud between the colonists,
erupting into violence as a huge sandstorm hits,
shattering the base and leaving them defenseless
against the deadly creatures of this world. They
must deal with the feud and repair the facility—or
find another way to survive—before these terrors of
nature tear them all apart.
WHAT’S THE STORY, MOTHER?
Heading towards your destination, you receive a video
call from Gaius aboard UNCSS Ìyánlá.
“Gorham Colony KOI-2650.01 is a mining colony.
Established 2067. Terraformed. Our records show the
planet is rich in pentlandite, iron ore and some trace
elements. The population in 2100 was noted as one
million. Founded by J.V. Gorham. Site of the deepest
drilling, apparently, at 23 kilometers. Was introducing
non-indigenous life to help with mining operations.
Earth standard gravity, orbits a red giant star with a
diurnal length of 36 hours. Arid with high winds and
frequent sand storms.
That’s all I have for you. As you know, our mission is
first and foremost exploratory and humanitarian—see
what’s there and if anyone needs immediate assistance—
then establish contact with any political authority and
negotiate their return to the United Nations’ fold. If
there’s no one there, assess the planet for immediate
recolonization and don’t forget to recover the colony’s
long data disc so we can analyze their history. You will
need to file a Colony Potential Report—I’m expecting
your assessments of future mining potential, scientific
research opportunities, any local life that’s worth inves-
tigating, and of course, any ad hoc opportunities for
scientific, commercial or financial benefit.
You will report your findings back to me. Hail and
farewell!”
176
W H AT I S G O I N G O N ?
The surviving colonists at the Tontas Ravine mining
facility, the Morino and Parks families, are old
enemies, who put aside their vendetta and worked
together out of necessity, to survive. After the Isola-
tion they continued to mine pentlandite—a common
ore they traded with other colonies.
Over the years that trade dried up, leaving them
struggling to survive. Twenty years ago tensions
flared, as did the feud. José Morino, the elder
brother to Emilia, Diego and Danny, was shot dead
by Patrick Parks. Patrick had sought revenge for the
loss of his family at José’s hands some years prior.
Realizing that feeding the vendetta would see
them all dead, those left behind called a truce and
tried to work together. Despite their differences,
they have only survived thanks to this collaboration.
Over the years they have collected a fortune in
precious stones, but the gems have no value unless
they can reconnect with civilization.
However, long-standing resentments and
hatreds are always just under the surface, and both
Diego Morino and Patrick Parks still harbor ice-cold
dreams of vengeance.
The last people to visit Tontas Ravine before
the PCs were Gorham’s Marauders, one year ago
(page 144). They found the NPCs’ ship, HMCSS
Janku, and wiped the navigation data from its
memory banks.
Then the PCs arrive. Suddenly both the Morinos
and Parks see a new future of luxury after so much
misery. But there’s no way they are going to share it
with their oldest enemies, who necessity made allies
but now are just getting in the way. Under the cover
of a terrible sandstorm Danny Morino is murdered,
and the feud is let loose once again.1 0 .
E X P E D I T I O N S
GORHAM COLONY’S
LONG DATA DISC
When the colony started to collapse the grand-
mother of the Morino siblings, Shaniah Morino,
collected the colony’s long data disc for posterity.
It now sits gathering dust in the basement vault at
Tontas Ravine. If the PCs ask the NPCs about it they
will be told where it is, and can be escorted there
to retrieve it, witnessing the way to access the vault
and the other treasures it contains.
CLUES TO
T H E M E TA P U Z Z L E
The PCs can find the first campaign clue (page
162) during this expedition, by learning from
the NPCs that another vessel had been here a year
before, its crew of raiders leaving them and the mine
alone and only boarding the NPCs’ old Bison ship,
the HMCSS Janku, where they wiped the navigation
data from its memory banks. Checking the HMCSS
Janku’s log will corroborate the clue.
SOLAR SYSTEM
& COLONY RECORD
KOI-2650 System and KOI-2650.01
KOI-2650.01
KOI-2650.01 is an arid Earth-like planet orbiting a red
giant that gives a pale rusty-orange tinge to every-
thing. Daily temperatures only reach 10 °C, and not
quite freezing at night. It has a long diurnal cycle of
36 hours, with little axial tilt so day and night are both
18 hours long (three Shifts). The storms swirl contami-
nated dust into the air—anyone breathing it will suffer
the effects of suffocation every Turn, or after any
strenuous activity (page 110 of the core rulebook).
The planetary map gives you all the details you
need for KOI-2650.01 should your PCs want to
further explore or even colonize it, using the rules
in the Appendix: Building Your Own Better World
(page 275).

1 77G A M E
M O T H E R
S E C T I O N
KICKING OFF THE ACTION
The action starts with the PCs aboard their SEV, scan-
ning the planet. In between the frequent storms, they
can make out the remains of isolated settlements
across the planet’s harsh, red-tinged landscape. All
of them look industrial and mechanized, pipes and
smokestacks, tanks and containers, all covered in dust.
None of them look anything other than deserted and
derelict.
If the PCs issue a radio call, they will get no reply—
the Morino and Parks families will hear them but have
learned to be cautious. They will wait at the facility to
see what the PCs do. However, they cannot hide the
heat signature and electrostatic noise Tontas Ravine
gives out.
The PCs can pinpoint the location, in the middle of
a vast rocky plain, cracked like a broken pane of glass
with ravines, chasms and canyons. A fly-over reveals
the facility, tucked neatly at the bottom of a wide
ravine. It has power, and on the plain above there’s
the glint of solar panels and the whirring of windmills.
About 500 meters away along the ravine rests the
derelict remains of an old Bison-class ship next to
what looks like a crude access ramp to the ravine floor,
big enough for a Daihotai 8×8.
It is impossible to land inside the ravine, and land-
ing near it is dangerous due to the uneven and broken
ground (−3 modification to PILOTING ). Landing next to
the Bison is easy enough, but still requires a PILOTING
roll. A failed roll means the ship has landed heavily,
taking D3 points of damage.
S H O R E PA R T Y : Tan Blatchman, the ICC Inspector
aboard the Solovetsky Island (page 159) demands
to come planet-side with the PCs, to see firsthand how
they go about applying ICC protocols in the field. He
will not cope with danger well and will need protect-
ing. Possibly an opportunity for the PCs to get rid of
their troublesome inspector, if they wish to do so.
T H E C A L M B E F O R E T H E S T O R M : When the
PCs arrive at the mine, they see six people waiting
to welcome them: Emilia, Diego and Danny Morino,
and Morgan, Violet and Benny Parks. Maya Morino
and Patrick Parks have taken their WY-37B Transport
Sled (page 146 of the core rulebook) to make a food
gathering run 100km to the north. They are all armed,
except Benny, but cautiously wary rather than threat-
ening. Emilia leads the conversation, saying they don’t
see a lot of folks around these parts, these days. She
178
will demand to know who the PCs are, where they are
from and what they are doing here.
It’s up to the PCs how they convince them they are
there to help, but when they explain they are a rescue
mission from Earth there will be a moment of dawning
realization on the NPCs’ faces—more than relief or
excitement, as they all realize their lives are about
to change dramatically, and they don’t need—don’t
want—the other family anymore. The PCs can notice
this dawning realization with a successful OBSERVA-
TION roll, but if questioned the NPCs will simply say
they are relieved that help has arrived.
This is an opportunity for the PCs to question the
Morinos and Parks, explore the facility and learn about
the history of Tontas Ravine. They should also learn
about the Gorham’s Marauders’ raid of the previous
year, and the NPCs can bring up their agendas with
the PCs, and see how they react.
T H E S T O R M : After the PCs’ arrival, and at a point
to best build the tension, a huge dust storm brews up
and brews up fast. The following happens:
They receive a call from their pilot “Dudge” (page
157) aboard UNCSS Solovetsky Island. He reports
that a storm is incoming, that it’s close and it’s big.
The PCs are too far away for recovery before it hits, so
Dudge is taking the ship into orbit to avoid damage.
Emilia Morino tells the PCs they can weather the
storm in their storm shelter, for staying outside could
be fatal. Any PC who insists on staying outside the
storm shelter suffers an eight Base Dice, Damage 2
attack from the dust, winds and falling debris each
Turn until the storm blows itself out one Shift later.
The other NPCs disappear to secure the facility as
best they can before the storm hits.
Benny Parks takes the opportunity to confront
Danny Morino about the affair with his mother. They
scuffle outside Danny’s pod, and Benny hits Danny
with a wrench. In a panic Benny drops the bloody
wrench and leaves Danny, unconscious, where he fell,
where the storm will kill him, but not before stealing
Danny’s keycard to the vault and hiding it inside his
boot. He dashes to the storm shelter, in a sweat.
As the storm hits and Danny doesn’t appear at the
shelter, Violet becomes distraught. If the PCs don’t
intervene, Benny holds her back while Morgan Parks
seals the shelter hatch. Violet punches Morgan, accus-
ing him of leaving Danny to die, and the PCs will learn
of the affair.1 0 .
E X P E D I T I O N S
179G A M E
M O T H E R
S E C T I O N
T H E E S C A P E : The storm lasts one Shift and
destroys the water tanks, flooding the basement and
the access tunnel to the storm shelter, from which
the PCs must escape. The shelter’s roof hatch opens
upwards. It’s stuck by the weight of water above it
and needs a firm push to force it open. When opened,
water will immediately gush into the shelter (+1
STRESS LEVEL to all), but if they let go of the hatch the
weight of water will close it, trapping them but stop-
ping the flood. Once the hatch is fully open it will take
the water two Rounds to completely fill the shelter.
When fully submerged, the PCs will need to make
drowning tests each round (page 110 of the core
rulebook) until they escape. They may plan their
escape before they open the hatch, in which case they
act in whatever order they have agreed. Otherwise,
draw initiative to see who goes first. Each PC needs to
make a successful MOBILITY roll to escape, but if they
fail, they are stuck for the Round and are blocking
the access tunnel. Those behind are stuck unless they
make a CLOSE COMBAT roll to drag the blocking char-
acter back down and out of the way.
T H E A F T E R M AT H : The storm has done terri-
ble damage:
T The base is dark and silent, with no power—only
gloomy red sunlight seeps in.
T The water tanks collapsed, smashing the Parks’
T
T
T
T
T
T
house and leaving a gaping hole running from roof
to foundations.
The giant door to the Harvester kennel is battered
and standing wide open, the Harvester nowhere to
be seen.
The vehicle bay has collapsed, and the tractor
is lying on its side badly damaged, at least one
rugged tire shredded and useless. Any vehicle the
PCs brought with them is equally smashed.
The comms aerial, that should be standing atop the
comms array on the southern cliff, hangs over the
precipice, held by a tangle of cables.
There is no way to contact the SEV now, with the
base comms out of action and the storm still raging
in the upper atmosphere, effectively jamming the
PCs’ own comms.
The windmills are bent and broken—some missing
entirely—but many still stand and look like they
might be operable.
Violet Parks is desperate to find Danny Morino, in
the hope that he is safe.

E X P E D I T I O N S
EMILIA M O RIN O
Responsible, considerate, and caring, the 43-year-
old Emilia still misses her brother, José, killed nearly
twenty years ago by Patrick Parks. She is convinced the
Parks will make some kind of aggressive move against
her family, and try to take the stash of gems, and
the claim, for themselves. She fears the unnecessary
suffering this will cause when everyone can be rich as
Croesus. Emilia will try to keep her brother, Diego, calm,
but wants the PCs to take charge and keep the peace.
STRENGTH 3, AGILITY 3, WITS 4, EMPATHY 4
HEALTH: 3
SKILLS: Command 3, Comtech 1, Heavy Machinery 2,
Manipulation 2, Mobility 1, Piloting 1, Ranged
Combat 1
GEAR: Protective clothing (Armor Rating 2), 37A2
shotgun, vault keycard, hologram of José Morino
DAN NY M O RIN O
DIEGO M O RIN O
Selfish and lazy, the 29-year-old Danny is not
liked by his older siblings, and over the years they
have given up trying to get him to be responsible.
He has read all the histories on life before the
Isolation and wants that for himself—he doesn’t
care who he tramples to get it. His love affair with
Violet Parks was a bad mistake. He immediately
sees that the PCs’ arrival will set-off the bloody
feud once again and wants to stay out of the
crossfire. He will ask the PCs for a job.
STRENGTH 3, AGILITY 4, WITS 3, EMPATHY 5
HEALTH: 3
SKILLS: Comtech 2, Heavy Machinery 1,
Manipulation 2, Ranged Combat 2
TALENTS: Husbandry (page 49).
GEAR: Protective clothing (Armor Rating 2), an
old Weyland Corporation chit for a return flight
to Earth, 37A2 shotgun
Quiet, angry, and vengeful, Diego, 39, cannot
shake the vision of his older brother, José, dying
before him, having been shot by Patrick Parks. He
has never forgiven the Parks and now it’s time for
them to pay for what they have done. With murder
in his heart, Diego will try to cut a deal with the
PCs for their help against the Parks but is deter-
mined to kill Benny so Patrick Parks will suffer.
STRENGTH 4, AGILITY 3, WITS 3, EMPATHY 4
HEALTH: 4
SKILLS: Close Combat 1, Comtech 1,
Manipulation 1, Medical Aid 3, Mobility 1,
Ranged Combat 2
TALENTS: Hothead
GEAR: His father’s old .357 Magnum (one
reload), medical kit, protective clothing
(Armor Rating 2)
181G A M E

S E C T I O N
M O RGAN PAR KS
Outwardly calm and content, but seething inside,
49-year-old Morgan knows his wife, Violet, is having
an affair with Danny Morino. Knowing that his father
Patrick will want revenge on the Morinos, he will argue
to have his father recalled as soon as the storm passes,
and they repair the communications equipment. He
will tell the PCs they cannot trust the Morinos’ word,
and the PCs should work with the Parks family alone,
hinting at a nice cut for them if they comply.
STRENGTH 3, AGILITY 3, WITS 5, EMPATHY 3

GEAR: Protective clothing (Armor Rating 2), M4A3
pistol, combat knife, vault keycard
VIO LET PAR KS
B EN NY PAR KS
No-nonsense, manipulative, and argumentative,
42-year-old Violet works as a roughneck and Har-
vester handler. Married to Morgan, she has been
having an illicit affair with Danny Morino for months,
right under her husband’s nose. She’s in love with
Danny and wants to take their share of the fortune
and escape this place. She needs the vault keycard
Morgan has and won’t let him stand in her way. She
will try to gain the PCs’ sympathies by making up
lies about Morgan’s abusive treatment of her.
STRENGTH 4, AGILITY 4, WITS 4, EMPATHY 4

Mobility 1, Manipulation 3, Stamina 3
TALENTS: Husbandry (see page 49)
GEAR: Protective clothing (Armor Rating 2),
heavy wrench
18 2
Kind, naive and easily agitated, Benny, 18, has a
sunny disposition despite the constant bickering
between the families. He just wants everyone
to get along and for the PCs to make everyone
friends again. He’s not clever and isn’t trusted
with any responsibility. He hates that Danny
Morino and his mother are having an affair and
decides to have it out with him—this turns into a
violent argument just as the storm hits that leads
to Danny’s death.
STRENGTH 3, AGILITY 3, WITS 2, EMPATHY 5

SKILLS: Close Combat 2, Comtech 3, Mobility 1,
Stamina 1
