Danny Morino’s vault keycard1 0 .
E X P E D I T I O N S
T O N TA S R AV I N E
The ravine walls are 40 meters high and sheer. They
cannot be climbed (although an enterprising player
with a Harpoon Grappling Gun can give that a try, with
a successful RANGED COMBAT roll to shoot the grap-
pler, and a MOBILITY roll to climb up).S O L A R FA R M : The solar panels often get clogged
with dust which stops them working. It takes one
person a full Shift to clean them all off, but once
complete, the power will come back online, as long as
there’s sunshine.
H M C S S J A N K U : The ship, 500 meters east along
the ravine, is not space worthy and has been left to
gather dust. Leggy-snakes (page 189) have nested
in it, but they won’t attack the PCs unless you feel it
adds to the scene. They skitter and slither and make
a noise that should be used to up the tension. There
is just enough power left to fire up the computers, so
the PCs can download the logs and see what Gorham’s
Marauders did to the ship (the first clue of the cam-
paign, see page 162).F I E L D N O D E S : The field nodes transfer power from
the solar panels and mini-mills to the rest of the base,
as well as power the pylons to create the electric field
that repels the insect swarms. If a field node is broken,
it will take a COMTECH roll and a Turn of work to fix.
O R E P R O C E S S I N G P L A N T : Ore is dropped into
a huge hopper that produces nuggets of pure pentlan-
dite, then automatically packaged and stored in the
warehouse. If the machine is on and someone falls into
the hopper they are killed.
V E H I C L E B AY : There is room in the bay for the
facility’s Daihotai 8×8.
M I N I N G S T O R A G E : This huge storage bay con-
tains twenty seismic charges (Blast Power 10), four
power packs (Power Supply 2 each) and five portable
air canisters (Air Supply 3 each). Additionally, it
will have anything that the players can reasonably
convince you would be in the warehouse of a frontier
mining facility.
T H E H A R V E S T E R K E N N E L : Built to contain the
Harvester, this structure is of the toughest materials
available but will be difficult to repair (HEAVY MACHIN-
ERY at −3 and a Shift of work). The adjacent storage
shed has five electro-prod “zappers,” and three power
packs with Power Supply 3 each. It also contains the
remote switch (Power Supply 1) that detonates the
electric charge attached to the Harvester’s harness
to subdue it. To activate the switch requires a Power
Supply roll, a successful COMTECH test, and to be
within MEDIUM range of the beast. The attempt can
be repeated if failed. If successful, the Harvester
will be subdued and not act for a Turn unless it suf-
fers damage.
F I E L D P Y L O N S : The pylons create a 20-meter-
high flickering electric field that encircles the top of
the ravine and defends against the native insects. If
any of the pylons are broken, the field cannot work.
A repair takes a HEAVY MACHINERY roll to realign
the pylon (taking one Turn), then a COMTECH roll to
re-connect it with the field (another Turn of work).
Once activated, anyone touching the field will take
a twelve Base Dice attack, Damage 1. However, if the
target takes no damage whatsoever, the field has
flickered, and they have passed safely through (a
desperate PC may try this if the only other option is
being eaten alive by the Swarm).
C O M M S A R R AY : This needs to be online for any
communications with the SEV or the Cargo Lifter. If
the aerial is broken, it needs two people to manhandle
it back into place, with a successful STAMINA roll and a
HEAVY MACHINERY roll to repair it, a job that will take
a Shift to complete.
L I F T T O W E R S : The towers are made of thin scaf-
folding, with an elevator that works when the base has
power and a rickety set of steps.
M I N I - M I L L F I E L D : Used to generate power but
susceptible to storm damage.
T H E M I N E : The tunnel runs for 100 meters before
it opens into a circular strip mine with concentric

BASEMENT
After the storm has passed through the basement is
flooded to a depth of one meter, bringing a −1 modi-
fication to MOBILITY rolls for moving through it. After
the storm, five leggy-snakes, that were nesting under
the water tanks, have been washed into the basement.
An OBSERVATION test will spot the ripples they make
on the surface of the water as they swim about. They
will try to bite anyone who lingers in the water but
won’t leave the water and expose themselves to
potential predators.
M41A Pulse Rifle (one reload) and two M4A3 Pistols

The long data disc for Gorham Colony is here. Spend-
ing a Turn to analyze the records reveals the following:
The population in 2100 was 120,000, with an
export/import economy reliant upon regular trad-
ing for food and other basic supplies.
Trade collapsed after 2100. Many colonists left
but those that remained—25,000 in 2150—could
survive.
In the 2150s, a decade of extreme storms and
the unchecked spread of insect swarms led to
much loss of life, and many more colonists died or
departed.
From about 2160, trading vessels from other colo-
nies stopped coming, and only a few isolated settle-
ments survived. The population was 350.

There’s no technical reason why the solar farm isn’t
delivering power, it must be dust (see Solar Farm).
One third of the mini-mills are still working but
there’s a short circuit at the northern field node
stopping the power reaching the base (see
Field Nodes).
The field pylon to the west of the northern field
node has collapsed, and the electrical field cannot
be activated (see Field Pylons).

T H E R E A C T O R : This has been turned off for
months due to a minor radiation leak, but it can still
operate. To bring the reactor back online, the PCs
need to devote a Turn of work, install fuel rods with a
HEAVY MACHINERY roll (if this roll is failed, all within
SHORT range take D3 Rads, but may try again), then
make a second HEAVY MACHINERY roll to fire up the
reactor. Once running the power is restored, but the
reactor emits Weak radiation (1 Rad per Shift) that
affects the entire facility.

EVENTS
P O O R D A N N Y : After the storm has passed
Danny is dead, lying outside the ground floor door
to his pod. He will be found by Violet Parks if the
PCs do not look for him. She will be hysterical at
finding her lover dead. He’s been scoured by the
dust and his skin flayed (+1 STRESS LEVEL to all
viewing him). He also has a severe head wound.
A MEDICAL AID roll will identify that the head
blow didn’t kill him, and an OBSERVATION roll will
find the bloodied wrench nearby. If his body is
searched, the PCs will find that his vault keycard
is missing (if the PCs don’t search him Emilia
Morino will do it and announce this news). The PCs
should have the chance to start investigating what
happened.
T H E F E U D E R U P T S : Eventually the feud
erupts into a violent argument between the Parks
and Morinos. The history comes out, leading to a
murderous fight between the families as they each
accuse the other of killing Danny to get the second
vault keycard (unless the PCs intervene). Diego
Morino will try to kill Benny, Violet Parks will try to
kill Morgan, then defend Benny from Diego. Those
left standing after two Rounds will scatter across
the compound to avoid being killed but will hunt
down their enemies as the scenario progresses.
How the PCs react will influence the outcome.
A N O T H E R O N E B I T E S T H E D U S T : At any
time you should feel free to add in the death or
confrontation of any of the NPCs, to heighten the
tension as the story progresses.
C O M I N G F O R T H E P C S : If either of the fami-
lies gets the upper hand in the feud, they start to see
the PCs as a problem, for they will have witnessed
murder. They will try and get the PCs to keep quiet
about the events here, either agreeing to pay them or
by persuasion. If this doesn’t work, they will try to kill
the PCs to keep their secrets safe.
A V E N G E F U L H A R V E S T E R : The Harvester
(page 318 of the core rulebook), still wearing its
harness, is out there somewhere, on the prowl. It’s
angry and resentful. When a character ventures
outside, the Harvester will detect the tremors
caused by their footfalls and track them. It will
attack if it gets the chance but can be distracted
by noise or other vibrations. If things need liven-
ing up, it will attack the main base in an attempt
to get at its tormentors.
E X P E D I T I O N S
THE LEGGY-SNAKES
These indigenous critters resemble a cross between
a cobra and a giant centipede.
SPEED: 1
HEALTH: 1
SKILLS: Close Combat 4, Mobility 10
VENOM: The creature bites with a base Damage
of 1. Its venom acts as a disease of Virulence 6 but
Sickness rolls are made every Turn instead of every
Shift. Using a dose of anti-venom immediately
stops the effect.
N I G H T FA L L : Night will fall at a time best
suited to the drama, and Tontas Ravine will be
plunged into darkness. Until the PCs restore the
power, they will need flashlights (with power) to
see anything, and still suffer a −2 modification to
OBSERVATION .
T H E C A R G O L I F T E R R E T U R N S : This
event should be played towards the end of the
story after the Swarm has been detected (see
Finale), to raise the tension at the worst possible
moment. The Cargo Lifter (a WY-37B Transport
Sled, see page 140 of the core rulebook) appears
and makes a hasty landing. Patrick Parks steps
from the cockpit pod. He has his gun drawn. Maya
Morino has been beaten and is restrained with
cable-ties. Patrick Parks says: “I’m flying us out
of the way of that damned swarm, but you’re not
all welcome. Parks only get aboard, or the little
Morino girl dies here and now!” He says he will
spare Maya’s life if the others comply, but he has
no intention of doing so (the PCs can make an
OBSERVATION roll to detect Patrick’s lie).
T H E F I E L D M A L F U N C T I O N S : The protec-
tive field goes offline. A COMTECH roll made from
the Control Deck or the basement Power Systems
will show them that one of the northerly field
pylons is faulty, preventing the circuit from closing
and the field from working.
THE DEADLY HARVEST
The PCs can try to “wrangle” the Harvester using the
“zappers,” to control it and stop it attacking people
or causing more damage. However, this is very hard
without the Husbandry talent. See page 90 for
more on Harvesters and how to control them.

PATRICK PAR KS
Bitter and vengeful, the “Old Man of Tontas Ravine”
cannot forget that day when José Morino killed his
wife and left him for dead—he still has a vicious scar
on his face as a constant reminder. His vengeance
will be fulfilled when he takes Tontas Ravine from the
Morinos and sees them dead in the dust. Patrick will
try to cut a deal with the PCs, to overlook the “fate” of
the ­Morinos for a generous personal cut of the Tontas
Ravine fortune.
STRENGTH 2, AGILITY 2, WITS 5, EMPATHY 3

TALENTS: Merciless

FINALE
After the power has been restored to the base, the
weather warning alarm sounds in the Control Deck.
If the PCs study the radar, they see a large shadow
to the east—a huge swarm of “space locusts” (page
316 of the core rulebook) and it’s coming this way
(+1 STRESS LEVEL to all who see this). It’s difficult to
tell how long it might take to arrive, but if it makes a
beeline for them, it could be within the hour.
The swarm will finally arrive. You should time the
arrival for maximum effect, and the PCs should feel it
coming as they desperately work out how to survive.
If the electric field is active, the PCs will see that the
swarm is huge and will eventually overwhelm it. Each
Round, the swarm makes its signature attacks against
THE FIELD COLLAPSES
The flickering petrol-blue lightning field around
the clifftop is keeping you safe. But the swarm is
throwing itself at it, sudden and intense flashes
marking the electrocution of insect after insect,
a relentless, unending onslaught. The tall pylons
shudder under the assault. Then you hear it, a
wailing groan of metal as a pylon shudders. Some-
thing falls away, a maintenance panel maybe, or
19 0
the field. On a roll of 6, the swarm strips a pylon. Read
the sidebar The Field Collapses to your players.
S U R V I V I N G T H E S WA R M : The swarm is a 4
zone Swarm (page 316 of the core rulebook), Speed
4, Health 20, impervious to all attacks other than fire,
explosions, and electricity. Once inside the compound,
it will attack for ten Rounds before moving on, eating
through walls to get to living flesh. This is the end-
game, the final scene, but there are three ways to sur-
vive: hide inside the Harvester kennel (only if it’s been
repaired), hide underwater (if the PCs have enough Air
Supply), or get the hell out on the Cargo Lifter.
some of its shielding. But either way you watch
as the pylon crumbles under the attack. Its lights
flicker and go out. The reassuring blue glow of the
shield begins to stutter, then go dark, setting off
an almost instant domino effect around the entire
field. In that moment, and before your very eyes,
the shield is gone and the Swarm floods into the
compound…1 0 .
E X P E D I T I O N S
MAYA M O RIN O
Serious, focused and direct, 20 year old Maya is a pilot
and driver. She hates the feud even though she lost
her father, José, to it before she knew him. This is her
home, and she wants the mine to succeed. She doesn’t
want to leave after all the hard work they’ve put in and
wants the PCs to help them get back on their feet. She
only cares about her aunt Emilia and the hapless Benny
Parks and doesn’t want either to get hurt. She will use
force to protect them.
STRENGTH 3, AGILITY 5, WITS 3, EMPATHY 4
HEALTH: 3
SKILLS: Close Combat 1, Comtech 2, Mobility 2,
Piloting 3, Ranged Combat 1
GEAR: Flight suit (Armor Rating 3), combat knife
EPILOGUE
After the storm there is still a viable planet to re-col-
onize, should the PCs want to recommend that, and
possibly a fortune in gems to deal with. After their
report goes in, the PCs might be quietly approached
by a corporate executive with a proposal that they
should capture the Harvester for use elsewhere, or
specimens of the insect swarm. ■

W A Y
“We are all like the bright moon, we still have our darker side.”
—KAHLIL GIBRANI
The PCs find a primitive colony that has reverted to
corporate authoritarianism to survive—a group of
cliff-dwellers protecting themselves from those who
turned feral and prowl the jungle floor. The PCs find
simmering class tensions, deadly dangers in the jungle
192
and a group of refugees from the Children of the Two
Divines. The PCs must preserve the colony and protect
the survivors, before Mother Ma’Kayla of the Children
of the Two Divines arrives and demands the return of
her wayward devotees.1 0 .
E X P E D I T I O N S
W H AT I S G O I N G O N ?
KOI-784.01 is a world of tropical jungles and mesas,
with staggering cavern systems that fan out across
the world. The rich mineral prospects offered by these
caverns were so enticing it was inevitable a colony
would be established.
At its height, Dylan Colony was a thriving commu-
nity of 40,000 people. It struggled with the Isolation,
and organized society finally collapsed 40 years
ago. Many people dispersed into the jungle to fend
for themselves, becoming feral in order to survive.
Others, under the last remaining vestiges of Weyland
Corporation authority, clung to civilized ways from the
safety of towering plateaus, but living in constant fear
of the ferals.
Since then, the cliff-dwellers have developed a
quasi-corporate hereditary dictatorship, under the
descendants of the Weyland Corporation execu-
tives—a board of ten led by three chief executives
presiding over several hundred workers. These Wey-
landers live a life of relative luxury, keeping control
through possession of the few weapons that still work,
but simmering resentment lies just under the surface.
The ferals number in the hundreds and had been
flourishing on the jungle floor, living within the

Mingled with the stench of the jungle, the smell of
the phosgene is almost lost, but there is a linger-

This can be detected with an OBSERVATION roll,
and then identified as phosgene with a MEDICAL
WHAT’S THE STORY, MOTHER?
The PCs receive a video call from Gaius aboard
UNCSS Ìyánlá
Ìyánlá..
“Dylan Colony, KOI-784,01. Established by Eldridge
Dylan Sanchez in 2059 to take advantage of plan-
et-wide cavern systems that were ideal for mining
operations. Terraforming initially failed but was
successful on a subsequent attempt. In 2100, the
population was 90,000, mostly mining interests
producing gold, titanium, and hematite. The
planet is exceedingly hot and steamy, with daily
still-functioning atmosphere processor, occasionally
raiding the plateaus for fresh meat. But the processor
is slowly killing them.
Some years ago, in an attempt to kill the ferals
without a fight, the Weylanders deliberately tampered
with the atmosphere processor, setting it to release
low levels of phosgene gas. Denser than the air, this
poison has been building-up on the jungle floor, grad-
ually throttling the life from the ferals.
Two months ago, a Heliades-class J ship crashed in
the jungle. Twenty former devotees of the Children of
the Two Divines, fleeing the cult, begged for asylum.
Suspicious of these outsiders, the Weylanders none-
theless gave them sanctuary in a small, tented camp
on a promontory called Judgment Bluff. They were
given basic shelter and food but were not trusted. The
refugees, grateful for a place to live, have been con-
tent with their situation, so far. They are mindful of the
Ovomorph they know is in the hold of their crashed
ship but have no idea what to do with it. What they
don’t know is that Mother Ma’Kayla and the Children
of the Two Divines have not given up their search to
return their rebellious sheep to the flock.
AID roll with a −2 modification. A successful use of
a Pups device (page 93) will identify the gas.
For every Shift spent breathing this poison, a PC
suffers Mild hypoxia (page 91).
temperatures reaching 48 °C. Mountainous terrain,
with ravines and thick jungle, reportedly suffers
from electromagnetic storms and monsoon rains.
Gravity is Earth-like. The day is 20 hours long.
That is all for Dylan Colony. Remember our
mission mandate and your responsibilities. Your
Colony Potential Report needs to cover the poten-
tial for future mining operations, the status of
the atmosphere processor, any scientific research
possibilities, and the usual ad hoc opportunities
that you may uncover.”

KOI-784.01
KOI-784.01 is hot and humid. Daily temperatures
reach 48 °C and don’t drop much during the night.
Dominated by mountains, ravines, widespread
caverns and thick jungle, it suffers from frequent
lightning storms, intense monsoons and banks of
fast-forming fog. The gravity is Earth-like, and the
day is 20 hours long. Alongside the risk of phosgene
poisoning on the jungle floor, the PCs may suffer
heatstroke (page 91), at your discretion. The col-
onists are acclimatized, and do not suffer from this.
The planetary map gives you all the details you need
for KOI-784.01 should your PCs want to further explore
or even colonize it, using the rules in the Appendix:
Building Your Own Better World (page 275).

E X P E D I T I O N S
KICKING OFF THE ACTION
The action starts with the PCs aboard their SEV, in
the air above the colony, scanning the scene.
There is little sign of activity from high orbit,
but the PCs’ flyby of the Dylan Colony site reveals
much. The atmosphere processor is still operating,
but the electrical flashes and the plumes of smoke
say it’s not in the best working order. All around it
lies the colony, overgrown and deserted, although
a few crumbled ruins still stand against nature’s
onslaught.
The jungle spreads in every direction, broken by
imposing rocky plateaus. At least 100 meters high
and very nearly sheer, the jungle hasn’t claimed
these mesas, and most are bare—except for the few
near the deserted colony. Taking a closer look, the
PCs can see that six of the plateaus are connected
by rope bridges. On those six stand rough buildings
and tents, smoke rising from small fires. And then
they see people—lots of people—hurrying from
their shanty shelters to look up into the sky, to
point, to shout. The PCs cannot hear what they are
shouting. It’s impossible to tell if they are terrified,
shouting threats or welcoming greetings.
L A N D I N G : The only easy option to land is within the
overgrown ruins of the old town, a few hundred meters
from the occupied plateaus, requiring a PILOT test with
a −1 modification. There is not enough room to land on
one of the occupied plateaus without blowing away
the entire flimsy settlement, but they could land on an
unoccupied plateau nearby, with a –2 modification to
the PILOT roll. They would then have to climb down, of
course. A failed roll means the ship has landed heavily,
taking D3 damage.
S H O R E PA R T Y : The security officer, Hamidah Amir
(page 158), recommends she accompanies the PCs
planetside, as the primitive society might present a
danger. She will be overprotective and see danger in
every shadow.
T H E A P P R O A C H : If the PCs travel through the
jungle to reach the plateaus, they will be stalked by
two ferals. Enter stealth mode.
F I R S T C O N TA C T : The cliff-dwelling colonists will
suspect the PCs of being either devotees of the Chil-
dren of the Two Divines or pirates on a raid. A group
of ten, including four guards, will warily approach
the PCs, and challenge them to identify themselves
and their purpose. It’s up to the PCs how they go
about gaining the survivors’ trust, but once they
have it, they will be invited to speak with their lead-
ers Vidan, Dzuma, and Yen. They will be taken under
guard to the roundhouse on the Enclave plateau,
escorted up the hidden tunnel and through the set-
tlement. They get a clear view of this place and its
people and the camp of the refugees. As they pass
here, Chikondi Okafor will attract their attention
and shout for help. Once at the roundhouse they are
greeted by the three chief executives, the rest of the
Weylander leaders, and Lespera. Vidan will welcome
them, explain the history of the colony, and ask for
support and supplies to maintain their lifestyle, and
weapons to destroy the ferals. The NPCs will try to
forward their own agendas.
THE JUNGLE
The jungle suffers from the phosgene gas—the closer
to the atmosphere processor the grayer the under-
growth, the more brittle the roots and stems. It is dense
and stifling, and moving through it is hard work. Any
attempt to run requires a successful MOBILITY roll, or
the PC catches on a root and falls prone.

TH E FERALS
The ferals have lived like vermin for 40 years, follow-
ing their instincts to survive. They can’t remember
when the urge to eat flesh became so overwhelming
that any flesh would do. That so many were seduced
by the same insanity made it more acceptable, and
soon it became the norm. Complete was their fall into
barbarism.
The ferals are wild barbarians, the apparent evil
nemesis in this story, but they are victims of the Iso-
lation too. The PCs can rescue them from their dark
path and get them treatment for their psychoses.
Until then, the ferals will be immediately hostile but
are weakened by the phosgene poisoning. If a feral
is captured, it may be possible to help them. The PCs
will need to make a successful MEDICAL AID roll with a
19 6
−2 modification, and a Turn of psychotherapy, to make
the feral cooperative and sufficiently trusting to allow
the PCs to help them. If not, they are too far gone, and
will need restraining and full hospital treatment to
have any hope of recovery.

FACE TO FACE WITH A FERAL
Beastly and savage, the feral moves with the graceful
intent of a tiger on the hunt, their eyes sharp and
reflexes at the ready. With blood-stained teeth and
cracked nails, scarred bodies, and ripped skin, they
carry their wounds proudly. They wear almost nothing,
torn rags tied in haphazard knots, but always hold their
weapons, their spears and bone knives, in readiness.
In that moment of calm, you see a flicker in their eyes,
of recognition, of humanity? And then they burst into
action, stabbing, swiping, grappling, to snare another
victim to be dragged screaming into the jungle.

better than the working life and want to keep it

DZU MA TIBANDI
WEYLANDER CHIEF EXECUTIVE
Old, indulgent, and kind-hearted, Vidan has led the
cliff-dwellers for years and enjoys the privileges
his rank brings. Sympathetic to Okafor and the
refugees, Vidan wants them to be accepted into
the community. The other chief executives, Dzuma
and Yen, disagree. Vidan regrets they could never
make peace with the Ferals, as there must be some
humanity left in them somewhere.
He wants the PCs’ help to make his community
safer. He will also ask if they know of the Children
of the Two Divines, as he wants to convince the
community to welcome the refugees. Whatever
the PCs say, Vidan will see the refugees as victims
needing his help.Impatient, ambitious and bloodthirsty, Dzuma
has long since decided she should be in charge.
The arrival of Okafor and the refugees, and now
the PCs, has given her the opportunity. She will
try to get the PCs to openly decry the primitive
state of their society and discredit Vidan. She will
also attempt to turn them against Okafor and the
refugees, again in her attempts to supplant Vidan.
To entice them she will offer any assistance she
can to help the PCs.

LEO NARD LES P ERA
Outgoing, caring but bitter, Lespera is the highly
respected leader of the workers. While he appears to
support the chief executives, he is angry at their deci-
sion to tamper with the atmosphere processor. It cost
two workers’ lives to the ferals to do it, and the workers
and jungle suffer for it. He has been quietly stoking
the growing resentment that is simmering against the
Weylanders. He genuinely likes Vidan and only this stops
him rebelling openly. If Vidan is removed from power or
harmed, Lespera will start the revolt.
He wants peace for the people but will hint to the
PCs that unrest is just beneath the surface.

YEN YAMADA
CHIKO NDI O KAFO R
REFUGEE FROM THE CHILDREN
OF THE TWO DIVINES
WEYLANDER CHIEF EXECUTIVE
Spoiled, vindictive and resentful, Yen wants to main-
tain the status quo but to rule alone. She enjoys the
rush of power, and neither Vidan nor Dzuma give her
the respect she wants. She sees the PCs as powerful
allies and will promise them anything if they assist
her in removing her rivals for power.

19 8
Selfless, hopeful but world-weary, Okafor cannot
now understand how he was swept-up by the
Children of the Two Divines. He has not seen a
Xeno­morph, the “Angel,” although he knows the
Ovomorph in his crashed ship has something to do
with it.
He has witnessed the infection that the Per-
fected spread, not least in Mother Ma’Kayla herself,
and all he wants now is a place to live in peace.
He fears Mother Ma’Kayla will come looking for
them, and desperately wants to find greater
safety—he sees the PCs as his way to achieve it.
Despite being under house arrest, he will attract
the PCs’ attention and beg for their help. If the
PCs ask about the Children of the Two Divines he
will trade his knowledge of the cult, and the Ovo-
morph in his crashed ship, in return for help and
protection.

E X P E D I T I O N S
M O T H E R M A’ K AY L A A N D
THE CHILDREN OF THE TWO DIVINES
Once the PCs have established themselves and
searched the crashed Heliades-class J ship, they will
hear another Heliades-class J vessel—this is Mother
Ma’Kayla. She has been hunting down Chikondi
Okafor and the refugees, desperate to capture them
alive and make an example by punishing them before
the cult. Tracking the ship’s transponder, she finds
Dylan Colony.
A R R I VA L : The PCs can see the ship circle the old
colony and the plateau, before landing on a plateau to
the north, near the location of the crashed ship. They
can’t make out any more details, but Ma’Kayla and her
devotees search the crashed ship.
C O N F R O N TAT I O N : The PCs will be confronted
by Mother Ma’Kayla and eight devotees, either at the
crashed ship (if the PCs choose to travel to investigate
the new ship’s arrival) or at the Weylander plateau (if
they choose to wait and see what happens). See the
sidebar Introducing Mother Ma’Kayla. If the confron-
tation plays out on the Weylander plateau Chikondi
Okafor will see Ma’Kayla and he and the refugees will
try to hide from her view, terrified of being found.
Ma’Kayla will introduce herself and say she is
searching for the crew (and cargo, if the PCs have
taken it) of the crashed vessel, as they are friends, and
asks if the PCs have seen them. If the PCs deny any
knowledge, or state the refugees are already dead,
she will simply nod. The PCs can tell she does not
believe them with a successful OBSERVATION roll. If
the PCs admit to knowing of the refugees Ma’Kayla
will demand that they be returned to her at once and
threatens reprisals if the PCs do not comply.
In the unlikely event that the PCs agree to hand
the refugees over Vidan and the majority of the Wey-
lander workers will vociferously disagree and prevent
this from happening.
Once the confrontation reaches deadlock Mother
Ma’Kayla will tell the PCs the matter is not resolved,
they cannot leave without her permission, and her ship
has orders to fire on the Solovetsky Island should it
attempt to leave (her ship is a Heliades-class J vessel
(page 75) armed with three light railgun turrets
and two Short Lance ASAT missile batteries—page 176
of the core rulebook). She and her devotees will return
to their ship.
INTRODUCING MOTHER MA’KAYLA
Tall and lithe, Mother Ma’Kayla walks with graceful
eyes don’t look at you, they look through you.
elegance. But she isn’t right. Her head is slightly
Composed and sure of herself, she stops before
too large, swollen and distended, her arms and
you, an almost mesmerizing sight. A slight smile
legs are bulky and just that little bit too long, her
plays across her lips.
THE CLIFF-DWELLERS’ CAMP
The camp is ragged, with buildings made from rough-
hewn wood and prefabricated panels and frames.
Tarpaulins keep the rains out. Old and rusted tools lie
alongside crude home-made replacements. Each of
the six plateaus has a giant wooden post projecting
twenty meters into the sky—primitive lightning rods.
The people on the plateau are fearful. Years living with
the threat of the ferals, and the daily terror that they
or a loved one might be dragged off to be butchered,
have cowed these folk and made them timid. However,
the arrival of the PCs is an enormous event. Everyone
is cautious, yet curious to get a look at the newcomers.
T H E C L I F F S : The cliffs are all sheer, and hard to
climb even with proper gear. Any MOBILITY attempt
comes with a −3 modification, with +1 for modern
climbing equipment. Two successful rolls are needed to
scale the cliff, each taking a Turn. Any failed roll and the
character plummets to the rocky ground, taking falling
damage as normal.

R O P E B R I D G E S : Twenty meters long and three
wide, these bridges appear rickety—any PC crossing
one for the first time must make a MOBILITY roll or
gain +1 STRESS LEVEL for the experience. But they are
surprisingly strong, and will take 12 damage before
they break, double damage from fire. Anyone on one
when it breaks must make a MOBILITY roll with a −2
modification to grab hold of something, otherwise
they fall the 100 meters to the jungle floor below.
T U N N E L : The tunnel is the only easy way up. The
entrance is hidden by an outcrop of rock, requiring an
OBSERVATION roll to spot from the ground, although
it’s easy to spot from the air. If the PCs fail to find it, a
party of cliff-dwellers will eventually make contact.
W O R K E R S ’ S H A N T Y T O W N : Only workers live
here, a busy and smelly place with an ever-present
sense of anxiety. Small cooking fires fill the air with
smoke as dogs and chickens run free and people move
between the shacks and tents that make this place so
crowded. A huge mound of laundry sits next to the
rain-filled pool, where the scrubbing workers sit up to
their waists. A guard makes sure no unauthorized folk
cross the bridge to the Bluff.
B L U F F : A few senior workers live here, but it’s simi-
larly busy to the Shanty Town.
FA R M : All the space here is used to grow food, with
tightly packed crops in small plots. A few chickens,
sheep and goats are squashed together in rancid
animal runs, and there is a sealed wooden Tarantula
farm, a dangerous but delightful delicacy.
S H R I N E : A large wooden gazebo, with a slatted
wooden floor, dominates one end of this plateau, faced
by a ring of huge stones. The craftsmanship is much
better than that found in the rest of the camp, and the
stones have been roughly carved to resemble human
figures. It’s uncanny, but the stone figures, as rudimen-
tary as they are, all seem to be crying out in desperation.
The community will come together at the Shrine to
decide the fate of the refugees from the Children of the
Two Divines. Vidan favors welcoming them as citizens,
but Dzuma and Yen don’t. Dzuma wants to cast them
out to fend for themselves, but Yen claims this will see
them become ferals. She demands their execution for
the safety of all. Okafor will plead for mercy, begging
the PCs to intervene on their behalf. If they don’t, Yen
wins the day, and the refugees will be thrown from
Judgment Bluff.
E X P E D I T I O N S
N A B O : The main trade and meeting plateau for the
community. Huts and tents hum with activity, from
tanning hides, making spears and slaughtering ani-
mals, to weaving clothes, firing pottery and crafting
crude jewelry.
M E E T I N G H O U S E : A sturdy long-house with a tar-
paulin covering the front to keep the rain off, a fire pit
that fills the center of the house and furs and blankets
lining the floor. It is used by the chief executives as a
meeting hall, court room, and feasting place. The PCs
will be invited to bunk down here during their stay.
J U D G M E N T B L U F F : Fenced off from the rest of
the Nabo plateau by a low wooden palisade, Judg-
ment Bluff is the community’s place of justice. Below
the twisted outcrop is a grove of plants that resemble
giant bamboo. Those guilty of any crime are thrown
from the outcrop to their deaths on the stakes below,
while the people watch. There are some bones at the
base of the cliff, but not many—before an execution,
a guard blows a long wooden horn that emits a rum-
bling note, calling the ferals to a free feast.
R E F U G E E C A M P : The refugees from the death cult
live here, in tattered tents. A guard always watches
them from behind the palisade.
E N C L AV E : Grand and well maintained, with sturdy
wooden buildings and better-quality furnishings, this
plateau is the exclusive home of the Weylander board
members. The chief executives live in the largest house,
on the south-east facing cliff. The colony’s long data disc
is here. If the PCs analyze it they will learn the following:
Dylan Colony continued to function for nearly 40
years after the Isolation, although many people left.
Unrest and political infighting saw the society
fracture in 2142.
2144 the mining operations ceased and the
facilities to the northwest of the colony were
moth-balled (instructions to re-start the facility are
recorded here).
2145 civil unrest running riot and collapse of
authority and civic control.

R O U N D H O U S E : This wood and stone building
serves as the Weylanders’ board room. Any matters
that require all the executives to contribute are dis-
cussed here. When the PCs first arrive, they will be
escorted here to receive the community’s hospitality
and speak with the chief executives.

M O T H E R
S E C T I O N
THE CRASHED SHIP
The Heliades-class J vessel was badly smashed in the
crash. The top two decks are an unrecognizable mass
of twisted metal and shattered trees. Access to the
ship can be gained through the torn hull on the lowest
deck via the vehicle bay. It’s partly swamped with mud
and earth from the jungle floor. From there it takes an
easy MOBILITY roll, with a +2 modification, to climb
the catwalks to reach the cargo hold.
T H E B R I D G E : This is hard to reach, needing a
MOBILITY roll with a −2 modification to squeeze
through the twisted wreckage. Once reached the PCs
see the systems are all destroyed, but it is still sending
out a transponder ping. They can turn this off.
T H E H O L D : The hold is a shambles after the crash,
with discarded baggage, shredded bags and papers
scattered all over. If the PCs search through the
papers, they find little of interest except a copy of
Mother Ma’Kayla’s letter to her devotees, the second
campaign clue (page 162). There are also three
small wooden crates. One is empty. The second has
been crushed by a falling beam, the Xeno­morph
egg inside it splattered and dead. It’s impossible to
retrieve it but the PCs could take a sample. In the third
is a live Ovomorph—it’s hibernating and does not
immediately open (see the event Wakey Wakey).
T H E AT M O S P H E R E P R O C E S S O R
The automated processes that have kept this place
running have been struggling for years, and it shows.
The rhythmic hum, hiss and clank of the machinery
is not right, and there is no way to access the under-
ground levels. Any PC with the HEAVY MACHINERY skill
will know that a major control hub should be located
on Platform 13.
G R O U N D L E V E L : The phosgene is most concen-
trated here, and everyone breathing it must make a
roll against its effects every Turn instead of every Shift.
A C C E S S D O O R : This huge door, set into the floor
of the processor, is open, revealing a 20-meter-deep
pit that would normally be used to access the lower
levels. However, it has long since been blocked off.
The pit has been used by the ferals to dispose of their
victims—the bottom is a gruesome display of rotting
humanity. Anyone viewing this gains +1 STRESS LEVEL .
P L AT F O R M 1 3 : The platform’s southern side has
a working control panel that will allow the PCs, with
a successful COMTECH roll, to adjust the atmosphere
processor’s output. The large service lifts on either
side of the platform work, with access ladders along-
side them.
The ferals use this platform as a nest, as exhaust
pipes constantly flood it with clean air. It is a shambles,
with shabby sheets on the floor and bones, sticks and
spears littered all over. At any time 15 ferals are here.
They will notice the PCs approach as they ascend to
the platform, and will hide amongst the debris, pipes,
and girders. Enter stealth mode. Once the PCs reach
platform 13 they will see the overwhelming number of
ferals, in a sudden and silent standoff. All must make a
Panic Roll.
As soon as a PC takes any action, or makes any
sound, all hell breaks loose. Five ferals attack, while
the others flee, spooked by the invasion of their nest
and shimmying down the beams and scaffolds. They
can be heard screaming and yelping as they escape.
T H E M I N I N G FAC I L I T Y
The facility was professionally moth-balled and
remains in good condition. The instructions to access
202
and restart the facility are contained in the colony’s
long data disc.1 0 .

EVENTS
I N A F L A S H : The weather changes in a flash—
literally. Lightning strikes the ground or a wooden
lightning rod on a random plateau. Anyone within
MEDIUM range suffers an attack with twelve Base Dice,
Damage 1. At your discretion this could set something
valuable on fire.
R O L L I N T H E F O G : Dense fog forms throughout
the jungle, reducing visibility to SHORT range. With
the fog the sounds of the jungle are deadened. An
eerie silence descends, only broken by the occasional
scrabble of something in the undergrowth. Everyone
gains +1 STRESS LEVEL . This may be a good prelude to
The Raiding Party event.
203G A M E
M O T H E R
S E C T I O N
T H E R A I D I N G PA R T Y : Suddenly from the jungle
undergrowth the PCs hear war cries and yelps of
excitement. A party of four Tomogo have smelled
them and want to snatch one of the group. They start
to hunt the PCs. Enter stealth mode. The Tomogo
intend to use their tried and tested tactics—they will
stalk closer before two will make a diversionary attack
at the front, while two others will use that distraction
to grab the tail-end charlie.
T H E WA N D E R I N G C H I L D : One of the devotee
refugees, Valery Reina, desperate to get some goat’s
milk for her baby, sneaks out of the camp in the
night and past the snoozing guard. The PCs get an
OBSERVATION roll to hear her as she crosses the Nabo
plateau. If they don’t, or choose not to act, she will
be caught on the Farm, creating a lot of noise. She is
dragged back by a guard and accused of stealing. If
the PCs don’t intervene, Vidan will regrettably pass
the death sentence on her, and she will be thrown
from Judgment Bluff, along with the inattentive guard.
WA K E Y WA K E Y : The Facehugger in the Ovomorph
wakes up and goes looking for a host at a moment
when the PCs are nearby, to create the greatest ten-
sion or trouble. If it is still inside the crate, the PCs will
hear a scrabbling noise for three Rounds before the
Facehugger bursts out. If the egg has been removed
from the crate, any PC within MEDIUM range can make
an OBSERVATION test to see or hear the egg open. At
your discretion it may attack the PCs, or impregnate
a nearby NPC. The cliff-dwellers will not react well to
this and may turn on the PCs as bringers of evil.
T H E F E R A L S AT TA C K : The ferals, agitated by the
invasion of their nest by the PCs, have been yelping
and calling in the forest, building for an aggressive
assault on the cliff-dwellers. Their calls can be heard
coming from all directions and getting closer and
closer to the plateau. All who hear this gain +1 STRESS
LEVEL . At the moment of highest tension, they will
appear at the base of the cliffs, and start climbing.
There are dozens of them.
T H E W O R K E R S R E V O LT : Tensions amongst
the workers reach breaking point, as it’s clear the
executives are using the PCs to feather their own
nests, while keeping the status quo. Led by Lespera,
the workers storm the Bluff and then the Enclave, to
demand equality. The executives will try to placate
them long enough to get them back to the Shanty
Town and defuse the situation, but—at your discre-
tion—the angry mob can grab the leaders and throw
them from Judgment Bluff.
FINALE
Mother Ma’Kayla’s patience wears thin. She contacts
the PCs giving them one last chance to hand the
refugees over. Her ship fires a warning missile that
just misses as a demonstration of her intent. If the PCs
refuse again, she says: “I regret you have forced my
hand and denied me my righteous retribution against
my wayward children. I have ordered my devotees to
overload the atmosphere processor. It will explode in
three hours, with the force of 15 mega tons. You will all
die. It is a pity, for you could have joined the Children of
the Two Divines and lived your lives in the glorious pur-
suit of perfection. If you attempt to leave, I will shoot
your ship down. If you wish to live, place the refugees,
alone, on the plateau by your shrine—leave them there
for us to collect. Once they are aboard you will be free
to depart. Don’t think you can repair the processor—
I have sent some friends to keep you occupied.”
20 4
Ma’Kayla has released two Stage IV XX033 Xeno­
morphs, Deacons (page 135), to cause panic and
fear at the cliff-dwellers’ settlement. They can be
heard squealing in the distance. Climbing the cliff is
no barrier to these monsters and they will raid the
plateau at a time to best enhance the tension.
It’s up to the PCs how they want to resolve this
situation. If they rush to the atmosphere processor,
they will have to cope with the ferals (although some
are dead, killed by the Children of the Two Divines)
and five devotees left behind specifically to prevent
the overload being deactivated. To deactivate the
overload requires a HEAVY MACHINERY roll, and a
Turn of work, followed by a COMTECH roll and another
Turn of work. If the PCs successfully achieve this the
Solovetsky Island will come under attack as Mother
Ma’Kayla tries to use force to recapture the refugees.1 0 .
E X P E D I T I O N S
EPILOGUE
Once the dust settles, literally or metaphorically, there
are still opportunities to re-colonize Dylan Colony,
should the PCs want to press for that. The Great
Mother Mission’s chief medical officer may be shocked
by the reports of the ferals and proposes a mission to
return to the jungle to find, capture, and treat those
poor people, and welcome them back into civilization.
But is there still a Facehugger running free? ■

2 05G A M E

3 .
S E C T I O N
L E A V E A L L E L S E
T O T H E G O D S
“We have a basic responsibility to our species to venture to other
worlds. Sailors on a becalmed sea, we sense the stirring of a breeze.”
—CARL SAGAN
The PCs are sent to a pristine planet, to colonize and
explore. But they are not the first to make landfall
here—they find the camp of a colony scouting team
stranded here 75 years ago. Under orders from Gov-
ernor Abantu, the PCs establish the new colony. But
as the colonists set up their new home, the PCs make
a terrible discovery—the ancient ruins of an Engineer
city, and the remnants of their genetic creativity. Can
the PCs uncover the terrifying secrets of the city in
time to save themselves and the new colony?
W H AT I S G O I N G O N ?
In 2100, just before the Isolation, a small survey crew
from Gorham Colony scouted the KOI-1966 system,
and found KOI-1966.03, the third planet. They nick-
named it “Aljanna” after the Hausa word for paradise.
They set up a forward base camp, but before the
planet could be colonized the Isolation changed
everything. The scouting crew soon discovered the
buried remains of an ancient Engineer city, and the
horrors that lay within.
When the Engineers fled this area of space thou-
sands of years ago, the city was abandoned in a hurry.
WHAT’S THE STORY, MOTHER?
The comms unit buzzes, the incoming ID code
showing it’s Gaius, calling from UNCSS Ìyánlá
Ìyánlá..
“Good day Solovetsky Island. I hope all is well.
As you know, a key element of the Great Mother
Mission is to re-colonize this sector of space under
the collaborative banner of the United Nations,
and not any one supernation or corporation. The
third planet in the KOI-1966 system, KOI-1966.03,
was noted as suitable for colonization before the
Isolation, and this has been corroborated by our
long-range survey scans. Governor Abantu has
taken a close personal interest in the colonization
of this planet—between you and me he is des-
perate for a good news story, and setting up the
20 6
They left behind the preserved remains of their cre-
ations—a form of proto-human, a primitive Arcturian,
a Fulfremmen, others now impossible to identify, and
XX121 Xeno­morphs.
The scouting crew disturbed the hibernating Xeno­
morphs and were quickly taken as hosts. Since then,
the hive has grown, the Xeno­morphs exploiting the
indigenous life on Aljanna and living in the dark halls
of the city.
first colony of the Great Mother Mission will be
that story.
Your task is to travel to KOI-1966.03 as the
advance party for the colonization. The Ìyánlá will
be 24 hours behind you. We have four atmosphere
processors riding on Ìyánlá’s back and consuming
fuel at a terrible rate, so we need to get them
deployed soon, and thousands of colonists on ice,
to wake up and start making better worlds for all.
You will oversee the colonization operation and
then survey the planet for valuable resources.
As I said, Governor Abantu himself is the driving
force behind this expedition and expects to see
rapid results. Don’t let him down.”1 0 .
E X P E D I T I O N S
C L U E S T O T H E M E TA P U Z Z L E
The PCs can learn the third campaign clue during this
expedition, by investigating the Gallery of the Ages
within the Engineer city and activating the Engineer
archives. The PCs will learn that the Engineers created
the Xeno­morphs and the Perfected but then could
not control them. They decided to leave this sector of
space behind, using a device they call “the Lychgate.”
KOI-1966.03—ALJANNA
KOI-1966.03—ALJANNA
KOI-1966.03 is a paradise world, a pristine twin
of Earth. It has a warm and temperate climate,
with tropical regions at the equator and freezing
poles. However, it does suffer from high levels of
ultraviolet radiation from the local star, equivalent
to Weak radiation that only takes effect once per
week—something an atmosphere processor can fix
by adding ozone to the stratosphere. Gravity is Earth
standard. The only significant difference is the day
length of 48 hours instead of 24.
The planetary details for KOI-1966.03—Aljanna—
are noted to the right and can be used to expand the
story of the PCs’ adventures on this world, should
they choose to continue the colonization once this
expedition has finished, using the rules in the Appen-
dix: Building Your Own Better World (page 275).

KICKING OFF THE ACTION
The action starts with the PCs arriving in the KOI-1966
system. They can learn about the system with a simple
survey scan, which also picks up a very weak signal
from an old colony pathfinder locator beacon on the
third planet. This is not a distress beacon but was
used by scouting teams to denote their presence and
a suitable location for colonization. It’s located in the
northern hemisphere (Northern Hemisphere West in
the diagram on page 207) in a region of mountains,
rivers and river deltas. If the PCs check, they can see
that this beacon is using a pre-Isolation code and is
thus at least 75 years old.
Further investigation reveals there is a small
prefabricated pre-colony base established on a wide
plain bordered by large rivers and a low mountain
range. There are no signs of human life and there is
no reply to any communication attempt. Their scans
also detect the following in the vicinity of the pre-col-
ony base:
A huge collapsed cliff-face, 25 km to the north,
radiating signatures for many rare and highly
sought after minerals. A successful COMTECH roll
will identify rhodium, iridium and platinum, a pros-
pector’s dream find.
A group of lakes, 50 km to the south, are blooming
with multicolored flashes indicating some form of
T
T
T
T
sea life: red, auburn, green, yellow, and orange—the
water is a painter’s palette gone mad. Perhaps
an indigenous source of food—just what a new
colony needs.
200 km to the northeast, the plains are filled
with beasts, herds of alien quadrupeds roaming
the landscape. A source of food, or creatures to
domesticate?
There is a large area of increased thermal signa-
tures 100 km to the east. A successful COMTECH roll
doesn’t give a clear answer but suggests this could
be either some low level volcanic activity, or a
cluster of lifeforms (it is caused by the underground
Engineer city).
It’s up to the PCs how they explore the planet. Landing
the Solovetsky Island anywhere requires a PILOTING
roll. If the roll fails the landing is still successful but the
ship comes down heavily, causing D3 damage.
S H O R E PA R T Y : The prospector on the Solovetsky
Island, Emily Quintana (page 158), insists she joins
the PCs planet-side to assist with prospecting and
surveying the environment. She will keep an eye out
for the PCs taking any finds and hoarding them for
themselves.
PRE-COLONY BASE CAMP
Sitting in the center of a three-kilometer wide grassy
plain, the camp consists of six prefabricated rigid
tents surrounding the pathfinder locator beacon, a
box one meter across with a series of aerials. It has
fallen on its side but continues to function, powered
by a grimy portable solar panel that stands next to it.
The camp has obviously been abandoned for a very
long time—the structures are smeared by ages-old
dust and dirt, containers and boxes lie scattered, the
grasses of the plains have grown around and through
the place. A battered Daihotai 8×8 tractor rests a few
meters away, slumped in upon itself with rotted tires
and its structure rusted and broken.
P R E FA B R I C AT E D T E N T S : One of the six rigid
tents has completely collapsed, and the others are
damaged. Some were torn open by the Xeno­morphs
20 8
when they claimed the last of the scouting crew—with
a successful OBSERVATION roll the PCs can detect that
some of the damage does not appear to be caused by
weather.
Despite the damage, there are many sealed boxes
of useful supplies—the PCs can find anything they
wish that would have been available in 2100, at your
discretion, unless it’s perishable, in which case it has
long since rotted away.
In one of the tents, amongst the camp debris, is
a data pad that belonged to the team leader, Daran
Bako. If the PCs examine it, they will find Bako’s
survey of this region, his clear recommendation that
it’s a perfect place to establish a new colony, and the
details of his last log entries. See the sidebar Daran
Bako’s Log.1 0 .
E X P E D I T I O N S
DARAN BAKO’S LOG
Daran Bako, expedition leader, Colonization Scout Team Delta-19, Aboki settlement, Gorham Colony
11/07/2109:Landfall on KOI-1966.03, henceforth called “Aljanna” for this planet is paradise.
12/02/2109:Initial surveys encouraging. This planet is ripe for colonization and this location
is superb, with access to plentiful resources within hundreds of kilometers. It’s
such a kind and forgiving world that some of my team are talking about giving up the
scouting life, and staying to set up the colony and live here.
01/11/2110:Our retrieval ship hasn’t arrived on time. Efforts to contact them are fruitless as
there’s some interstellar interference. Jamal suggests it could be a solar flare.
03/24/2110:Supplies are running low and still no sign of retrieval. The team is becoming
dispirited. We are having to cast our net further. This planet can certainly feed us,
we just have to get on with it. There’s potentially a verdant spot out to the east,
and we go to explore that tomorrow.
COLONIZING ALJANNA
The planet appears ideal for colonization, just what
the Great Mother Mission has been looking for. Once
the PCs have made their initial exploration of the
pre-colony base, they receive a message from the
Ìyánlá, that they are in orbit and will commence colo-
nization procedures in one Shift. As such, the PCs are
expected to proceed with colonization, by Governor
Abantu, Ìyánlá’s synthetic overseer Gaius, and the
other Solovetsky Island crew members—they not only
think the place is perfect for colonization but want the
distinction of establishing the first colony under the
Great Mother Mission, to be recorded for posterity as
founders, and get a fat bonus in their paycheck.
Colonization should take place before the PCs
find the Engineer city and the dangers that lurk there.
However, if the PCs are determined to delay coloniza-
tion for any reason, make sure they feel the full wrath
and displeasure of Governor Abantu who, if necessary,
will get the PCs on comms and give them a direct
order to begin the operation.
Once the PCs are ready to start the colonization
process you should use the guidance in the Appendix:
Building Your Own Better World (page 275), and
follow these steps:
1 The colonization will take place at the PCs’ loca-
tion, in the Northern Hemisphere West region of
the planet.
2 If any of the PCs have family in cryosleep aboard
Ìyánlá, they can choose to have them join the
colony deployment.
3 An advance party under Colony Supervisor Man-
isha Kiran arrives but the PCs and their crew are
expected to manage the operation to get the
machinery on the ground. This requires a Shift
of work and a HEAVY MACHINERY roll to control
each deployment of the atmosphere processor
and three colony modules (four rolls in total)—an
NPC crew member can make this roll if their skill is
highest. If the roll is failed for any of these, roll on
the table on page 210 to see how badly things
go south.
4 Once the colony is safely on the ground, the PCs
should roll for the colony’s starting attribute values
and Development Level (page 285)—then the
colony is ready to play.
5 In honor of Daran Bako and his crew of scouts,
Governor Abantu chooses to name the colony
“Aljanna.” Colony Supervisor Kiran and the initial
colonists celebrate this moment with the PCs.
Cartons of prefab meals and bug juice are cracked
open, backs are slapped and cheers ring out.
Governor Abantu contacts the PCs to congratulate
them, and everyone takes a moment to relish their
success.

COLLAPSED CLIFF
The cliff is 25 km north of the base camp. A landslide
over a kilometer wide occurred some years ago,
revealing in cross-section the mineral rich caverns and
tubules within. Some are natural, but many are caused
by a Harvester-like creature, a fact the PCs can learn
with a successful OBSERVATION roll. This constant
internal erosion caused the landslide in the first place,
and the remaining cliff is highly unstable.
It is littered with mineral ores, including rhodium—
exceptionally rare and vital for electronic systems and
fuel components, iridium—used to harden alloys and
as a catalyst, and platinum—ever in demand. A very
rich find and a powerful reason to colonize the planet.
The enormous mound of jagged scree at the base
of the cliff stretches along its 1,000 meter length. It
requires a MOBILITY roll to climb across. If this is failed,
the PC slips and falls on the sharp rocks, taking one
point of damage. They must also roll a Stress Die—on
the scree begins to slip. The PC and all within
MEDIUM range must make a MOBILITY roll or get swept
along in the small avalanche, taking an eight Base
Dice attack, Damage 1. Another Stress Die should
sees a 50-meter-
then be rolled—this time a roll of
wide stretch of the cliff start to come down with an
earth-shattering crack. All who witness this gain +1
STRESS LEVEL and must make a MOBILITY roll to avoid
the rock fall. Anyone caught in its path takes a twelve
Base Dice attack, Damage 2.
At your discretion, this disturbance may rouse D6
small Harvesters that were within the rock (treat them as
Harvester Juveniles, page 318 of the core rulebook). They
are angry at being disturbed and will attack the PCs.
ALGAE LAKES
A series of lakes linked by rivers lies 50 km to the
south of the pre-colony base, at the apex of a huge
delta. They are filled with multicolored weeds and
algae, mostly growing around the shallow edges of
the water, where it rarely gets deeper than 1.5 meters.
If the PCs wade into the water to reach the plant life,
they can take a Turn to analyze it with an OBSERVA-
TION roll:
For one
the PCs learn that the weeds and algae
are all edible.
For two
they assess they are fast growing and
are food for other creatures, as evidenced by the
T
T
21 0
T
coin-sized bites taken out of the weeds’ leaves. The
weeds have electrocytes within their stems that
create a low electric current, presumably to keep
the predators away.
For three or more
the PCs realize that these
species are symbiotic, that the weeds use the algae
for basic minerals, and the algae attaches to the
weeds to grow its spores.
The predatory creatures, Octobugs, also live in the
mass of weed-algae. At your discretion, any PC in the
water will be attacked by D3 of them.1 0 .
THE OCTOBUGS OF PARADISE
No bigger than an adult’s hand and tan in color with
three tentacles, each Octobug is equipped with
razor-sharp gripping claws. They gain sustenance
from a form of electro-synthesis, with the ability
to detect the warmth and energy from powered
systems and absorb it. They are easily agitated and
excitable. Usually found in small groups, they are
most dangerous when they act as a swarm.

OCTOBUG ATTACKS
D6ATTACK
1–2POWER HUNGRY: The Octobug makes an attack with eight Base Dice, Damage 1, ignores armor. If it hits, it
sucks D3 power from the Power Supply of a random item in the target’s possession. If the item is a compres-
sion suit, respirator or other breathing kit the power dips and the item loses D3 from its Air Supply instead.
3
SUFFOCATING: The creatures cover, fill or otherwise block the airways of their target. Attack with six Base
Dice, Damage 1. If any damage is inflicted the victim is grappled and suffers suffocation.
4
NECROTIZING VENOM: The Octobug attacks with six Base Dice, Damage 1. If the target suffers any damage,
they are bitten, jabbed, spiked or scratched with venom that starts to eat them from within, Virulence 8.
They must make a save every Turn or suffer one point of Damage until they resist, get MEDICAL help, or die.
5
GO FOR THE HOT SPOT: The Octobug targets the biggest source of power within SHORT range (this could be a
compression suit worn by a PC, or a vehicle), and makes an attack with six Base Dice, Damage 1. If the attack
hits the target suffers a huge power surge, sparks fly, systems fry, and the equipment shorts out completely
(if the target is a vehicle, roll on the Component Damage Table on page 115 of the core rulebook).
6
SWARMING CRITTERS: The Octobugs swarm and go for the kill, tearing, slicing and ripping at their target.
The victim takes an attack with eight Base Dice, Damage 1. Any damage mitigated by armor causes an extra
point of damage to the armor and may cause a sealed suit to tear (page 93).
THE ROAMING HERDS
If the PCs travel 200 kilometers to the northeast, they
find herds of alien bovine creatures, calmly grazing
the long grasses. An OBSERVATION roll will reveal the
grass to the rear and flanks of the herd rustling as
something unseen moves amongst the stalks. There
are three indigenous creatures, akin to Lionworms
(page 320 of the core rulebook), hunting the bovines.
The Lionworms realize the PCs are not prey and will
ignore them unless they get in the way of the hunt, in
which case one will attack, not to kill but to warn the
PCs away from the Lionworms’ meal.
If the PCs want to analyze the bovines, they can
either hunt one (Health 6, Armor Rating 2, MOBILITY 5)
or make a MOBILITY roll to get close and a CLOSE
COMBAT roll to grapple. Once grappled the bovine will
go limp and compliant. An OBSERVATION roll will tell
the PCs the following:
For one
the PCs assess that the creatures are
edible and have a silky woolen coat that would be
valuable for making textiles.
For two
they assess that the creatures are par-
tially mammalian—partially reptilian, and probably
lay eggs to reproduce.
For three or more
the PCs realize that these
creatures are docile and should be easy to
domesticate.

THE FLORA OF THE CITY
The Engineer city has become home to a species
of pink toadstools of the fungus Ophiocordyceps
vehemens. These sweet-smelling fungi live in
dark, dank places and can be found anywhere
in the city. They disperse invisible spores in
response to movement within SHORT range.
Anyone exposed must make a Sickness Roll
against Virulence 6. If infected, after one Turn
they will begin to exhibit angry outbursts at the
slightest provocation. Get your players to role-
play this and reward them with a Story Point for
good roleplaying.
After a Shift, the victim becomes enraged, goes
berserk against any living thing, fighting until
they or their victim is dead, Broken or they are
restrained. The victims do not eat or drink, so may
perish through dehydration or starvation (page
106 of the core rulebook) if they fail to recover
soon enough or are not restrained and given
medical treatment. A successful MEDICAL AID roll
adds a +3 modification to the victim’s subsequent
Sickness Rolls. A victim makes another Sickness
Roll every 24 hours, against Virulence 6, until they
succeed and overcome the disease, or perish.

E X P E D I T I O N S
ENGINEER CITY
The city is 100 km east of the base camp, and is
hidden beneath millennia of weathering and erosion,
as well as the growth of local plants and creatures. On
first examination the place looks natural, sitting on a
plain with semi-symmetrical mounds in the ground.
Outside this ring of mounds, the grassy earth rises
sharply until it meets the surrounding mountains and
cliffs. The view to the south, from the sheer cliff, is a
breath-taking vista of the planet’s awesome beauty.
Access to the area is either by air, or along a
500-meter-wide valley to the west.
The PCs can detect the slight increase in ambient
temperature here, either using the Solovetsky Island’s
scanners or with a Pups device and a COMTECH roll.
They cannot detect any obvious volcanic activity or
unusually large concentrations of animal or plant life.
M O U N D S : Grass-covered and wet, these mounds
cover ancient Engineer structures that are now just
archaeological relics. Excavation with a tractor or
digger will reveal these stony ruins.
R I V U L E T S : Rain running off the mountains has
turned the ground marshy, with a number of small
rivulets running down to a central hollow. Crossing
them is tricky, requiring a MOBILITY roll to avoid get-
ting stuck in the mud for one Round.
H O L L O W : The grassy ground here forms a hollow
bowl with a slushy pool of water at the bottom. This
ground has built up over the sliding iris-valve doors
that would have allowed a Juggernaut to dock below
ground. They are stuck open, hidden beneath this
unstable ground. Any disturbance—such as a PC
walking on it—risks a cave-in. Roll a Stress Die each
the earth liter-
Round a PC is in the hollow—on
ally falls under their feet, and they plunge into the
Juggernaut Bay. The hollow caves-in automatically
if a vehicle drives across it. Any PC that falls gains
+1 STRESS LEVEL , but only takes an eight Base Dice
attack, Damage 1, as their fall is slowed by the roots
and branches that fill the bay, and they land on the
buildup of mud at the bottom.
O P E N M O U N D : The earth mounds were formed
by the weathering of the site over thousands of years.
The open mound has had some of this earth taken
away by the Xeno­morphs, leaving a narrow tunnel in
the earth that accesses the southern Access Tower in
the Juggernaut Hub.

INSIDE THE CITY
The Engineer city has been empty
for many thousands of years, aban-
doned before the Perfected could
arrive and destroy it. It has some
residual power that illuminates
its tunnels and chambers with a
gloomy blue glow but is otherwise
shrouded in shadow. It smells
musty and damp, an odor of stag-
nation and decay.
The ceremonial parts of the
city—the Temple and Gallery of the
Ages—are acoustically designed
to carry and amplify the songs
of the dead Engineers but have
that effect on any sound made
within them.
Doors within the city are either
large stone edifices that can be
opened by pushing for one Round

J U G G E R N A U T B AY : Filled with mud and plant
growth, this place is musty and damp. The floor
consists of a huge iris-valve hatch large enough
for a Juggernaut to pass through, leading to the
Juggernaut Docking Cavern below. It is fractionally
open, leaving gaps in the floor half a meter wide—
just enough to squeeze through. The distance to the
floor is 300 meters, so the PCs will need plenty of
rope and a successful MOBILITY roll if they want to
rappel down to the cavern floor below. A failed roll
will see the PC get tangled in the ropes and stuck
dangling or fall the rest of the way to the cavern
floor, at your discretion.

A N T E C H A M B E R S : Huge empty rooms, once used

A C C E S S T O W E R S : Wide spiral staircases made of

J U G G E R N A U T D O C K I N G C AV E R N : This gigan-
tic circular chamber, 1,300 meters across, is big enough
to house ten Engineer Juggernauts—and five of these
enormous ships, old, cold, silent, empty, and long dead,
still rest here now, only accompanied by the lonely echo
of dripping water. This place is so awesome that anyone
viewing it for the first time gains +1 STRESS LEVEL.1 0 .

TEMPLE
The only way to access the Temple is from either the
Juggernaut Bay or Docking Cavern, all other routes
are blocked by rubble and years of decay. A pyramid
shape, the Temple’s ceiling is 100 meters high, rising
to 200 meters over the central altar-dais.
S I X S TAT U E S : Within the depressed area of the
altar-dais are six enormous head statues, 20 meters
wide by 50 meters tall. In the gaps between them are
carvings of various Xeno­morphs, looking as if they are
climbing and embracing the statues. All viewing this
must make an OBSERVATION roll to recognize these
are carvings—all who fail the roll are shocked and
surprised and gain +1 STRESS LEVEL .

above the temple floor, these are platforms once
used for congregations to watch and join the temple
ceremonies.

platforms, these give a better view of the temple.

THE ENGINEERS’ SONG
Your eyes are assaulted by the sudden blue glare as glowing
hieroglyphs flood the air before and around you, spinning and
swirling, dazzling your mind and your vision. Around these
arise tall figures, human but not human, chiseled as an ancient
statue but graceful as a ballet dancer. You watch as they take
up their instruments and play a hypnotic tune and wonder
as a horseshoe-shaped vessel rises from the floor, spinning
upwards and away, followed by another and another. Eventu-
ally the music stops, the figures laying aside their instruments
to watch as one last image, of a vast spinning structure before
a beautiful be-clouded planet, slowly fades into shadow.
21 6
T
C O N T R O L D A I S : An ornate array of
machinery and equipment is designed in the
shape of an orrery, with dark metallic arms
sporting globe after globe, in a complex
arrangement representing hundreds of star
systems. Four seats allow a PC to sit cross-
legged at the controls, each seat with a
vertical or transverse flute of either an upper
or lower key. If a note is played on all four at
the same time the dais bursts into life, and
blue holographic glyphs suddenly rotate
in the air. See the sidebar The Engineers’
Song. This is the third campaign clue (page
162). A PC can try to decipher the glyphs
with an OBSERVATION roll with a −1 modifica-
tion, or alternatively DA/UT/UR aboard the
Solovetsky Island can do it for them.1 0 .
C U LT I VAT I O N C H A M B E R S 1 & 3 : Used to grow
Engineer specimens, these chambers are empty.
C U LT I VAT I O N C H A M B E R 2 : In their rush to
evacuate, the Engineers left behind live specimens of
the XX121 Xeno­morph. Over the years they managed
to escape, opening the once sealed door just far
enough for a Drone to squeeze out and explore. Now
the hive fills this chamber. A Queen slumbers in the
shadows at the far end, her work laying Ovomorphs
done for now, as 100 eggs lie dormant before her. She
E X P E D I T I O N S
is guarded by two Praetorian Stage VI Xeno­morphs,
the three of them too large to ever leave the city. The
hive has five Stage V Soldiers, and many Stage IV
Drones and Scouts. They are all PASSIVE .
The PCs can see this through the observation
windows set either side of the ajar door. They gain +1
STRESS LEVEL and must immediately make a Panic roll.
If this doesn’t alert the Xeno­morphs to their presence,
the PCs must make an opposed MOBILITY roll against
the Xeno­morphs’ eight Base Dice, to avoid detection.
Enter stealth mode.
EVENTS
Ì YÁ N L Á C A L L I N G : If the PCs are taking their time
over deciding to colonize KOI-1966.03, they receive
a message from Gaius. Despite being a synthetic, a
faint hint of frustration can be heard in his voice. He’s
pressing for an answer on the colonization potential
of KOI-1966.03, saying that Governor Abantu “is
desperate to see progress, and his comments on it are
frequent and vivid.” He asks for an urgent progress
report and needs a very good reason why the PCs are
not getting on with it.
D E V I L S I N T H E D A R K : The Engineer city is home
to vermin, and they skitter away if they hear noises or
see lights from the PCs. They PCs will hear this. If they
go looking for the cause they can catch a glimpse of
a rat-like creature with a successful OBSERVATION roll.
However, if they fail to find the source, or don’t even
try looking for it, the constant noises in the distance
give them +1 STRESS LEVEL .
T H E W I L D L I F E O F A L J A N N A : When out in the
wilderness, the PCs are stalked by an indigenous crea-
ture akin to a Lionworm (page 320 of the core rule-
book). Enter stealth mode. When the Lionworm makes
its first signature attack, it instead rushes a random
PC, then stops. The PC gains +1 STRESS LEVEL as the
creature scrutinizes them, before deciding the PCs are
not prey. If the PCs resist the urge to be hostile it will
turn and calmly slink away into the undergrowth.
FINALE
Once the PCs have discovered the Xeno­morph hive,
things will move quickly. Even if the PCs successfully
sneak away from the hive, an alert Xeno­morph will
detect them before they escape the Gallery of the Ages.
The chase is on. Three Xeno­morph Scouts and three
Drones give chase, with many more following behind
them, at your discretion.
E S C A P I N G T H E C I T Y : The PCs can slow down the
Xeno­morph chase by closing the door to their cultiva-
tion chamber. Just closing it will only delay the Xeno­
morphs by D6 Rounds. If the PCs have a cutting torch,
they can do a rush job of welding it shut, with a HEAVY
MACHINERY roll with a −3 modification—a success will
delay the Xeno­morphs by a further D3 Rounds. They
can try again if this fails until their torch runs out of
power. However, while the PCs are doing this, the
Xeno­morphs will be trying to force the door open. To
resist this, the PCs need to succeed at an opposed
STAMINA roll against eight Base Dice.
Closing the slatted gates will also slow the Xeno­
morphs by another D6 Rounds per gate they have to
smash through. If the PCs manage to out-distance the
Xeno­morphs, in a vehicle or a ship, the Xeno­morphs will
give up and return to the hive.
217G A M E
M O T H E R
S E C T I O N
D E A L I N G W I T H T H E T H R E AT : Even if the PCs
escape the city, the threat to Aljanna and the newly
founded colony is terrible. The PCs could try to return
to the city to seal the Xeno­morphs inside, either by
sealing the internal doors, or collapsing the structure
in on itself with explosives, but this would come with
significant risk and the Xeno­morphs would oppose
it. Alternatively, they could try to convince Gaius
and Governor Abantu that the threat is so severe
they should use one of UNCSS Ìyánlá’s arsenal of
terraforming nuclear weapons, and nuke the site from
orbit—after all, it’s the only way to be sure. Abantu is
in favor, in order to protect and keep KOI-1966.03 as a
new colony prize delivered by the Great Mother Mis-
sion, but Gaius and Kamal Vartouhi of Weyland-Yutani
(page 170) are violently opposed to it. Gaius will
suggest they send an exploration team to check out
the PCs’ claims and offer the PCs the chance to lead it.
If the PCs are determined the site should be destroyed,
they can attempt an opposed MANIPULATION roll
against Gaius, with a −3 modification, to have him
relent and leave Governor Abantu clear to give the
order. It’s up to you how many, if any, of the Xeno­
morphs escape the blast…
EPILOGUE
The newly formed colony may need help getting on
its feet, and the PCs could be a part of that, exploring
and prospecting, or gathering much needed sup-
plies for the colonists. A Weyland-Yutani executive
may want to take advantage of the archaeology of
the planet, and proposes the PCs make a quiet and
unofficial return to the city—now better prepared—to
acquire samples and data that W-Y would pay hand-
somely for. ■
