THE CHALKED GLYPHS
These glyphs, chalked on the floor by the Per-
fected, are the third campaign clue, and are also
found in the Engineer city on KOI-1966.03 (see the
expedition Leave All Else To The Gods). Finding
S L E E P C H A M B E R : Filled with five rows of low
Engineer cryosleep cubicles, a total of 250. All are
open except for one, which contains the skeletal
remains of a millennia-dead Engineer. If the PCs open
it—with a COMTECH or HEAVY MACHINERY roll—a
gush of rancid air will assault them, and the body will
disintegrate.
At the far end of the chamber two open cubicles
are each occupied by a slumbering Fulfremmen
(page 126), blanketed by the fleshy tendrils of a
Proto-Hive Node. With a successful OBSERVATION roll
the PCs will notice that the Node’s tendrils are trying
to penetrate the ship’s structure, but cannot. On the
floor by the cubicles are what appear to be Engineer
hieroglyphs marked out in chalk. These are not the
same as those on the Guardian ship but are from the
ruined Engineer city on KOI-1966.03. See the sidebar
The Chalked Glyphs.
The Fulfremmen will awaken and calmly approach
the PCs, initially curious. See the sidebar The
Fulfremmen.
The PCs immediately sense a feeling of welcome,
images of togetherness filling their heads, and an
intangible call of “join us.” All PCs must make a test
against their EMPATHY (attribute only). If this is failed,
they are entranced, and cannot act until they succeed
at a subsequent test (made once per Round) or suffer
damage. The Fulfremmen will reach out to touch
those entranced, exposing them to the Perfected’s
THE FULFREMMEN
Tall, lithe, and majestic, the two Perfected approach
with grace and elegance. Their black eyes scan
the scene, heads tilting this way and that. Their sil-
very-gray skin shines in the blue glow. One of them,
with a crimson marking—a birthmark or blemish
sketching a “V” shape on its cheek—peers at you
intently. The other—similar in every respect except
the golden mottling of the skin of its neck and shoul-
ders—reaches out a hand. You feel something, an itch
in your head, in your mind. Then you see it—a gro-
tesque image of twisted figures writhing in an ecstatic
orgy of pain and joy. You feel the pull, the invitation,
to be one with the hive, to be one with perfection.
25 8
them scrawled here by the Perfected should allow
the PCs to connect the Lychgate with the Per-
fected and start their suspicion that the Perfected
may want to use it to travel to the Middle Heavens.
infection—treat this as a disease with Virulence 6. If
the Sickness Roll fails, the victim becomes a Stage I
Humanoid Abomination (page 123).
Once one or more PCs succeed at their EMPATHY
test, and resist the Fulfremmen’s telepathy, the Ful-
fremmen become resentful and bitter. The PCs now
sense a feeling of anger, images of violent retribution
filling their heads. The Perfected will attack. If Nessa
Majken is here she will be deliriously happy and offer
the Fulfremmen the data pad with the navigation data.
Gorham will fight to the death to stop this happening.
A M B U L AT O R Y : This 800-meter cylindrical passage
is 50 meters wide, its ribs and structures forming a
rough spiral that coils the entire length—an awesome
spectacle.
T H E S P I N E : A massive obsidian door stands ajar
between the Spine and the Ambulatory. Behind the
door, a multitude of narrow passages disappear in
all directions. Any PC venturing here must make an
OBSERVATION roll to find the way back, but for every
failed roll the next test is at a cumulative −1 modifica-
tion. Using a Pups device gives a +1 modification to
the OBSERVATION roll. If the PCs OBSERVATION dice
pool is reduced to zero dice, they are hopelessly lost
and will eventually die unless rescued from outside.
Two Stage III Revenant Abominations (page 123)
are within these tunnels and will surprise the PCs.
PABLO’S LAST WORDS
The journal charts the events that led to the destruc-
tion of Pelican Colony—the increased solar activity,
the flares and radiation bursts, the panic among the
people, and Bengochaea’s escape from his job at
the dam into the Skritio Caves. The last entry reads:
“About 30 of us have made it into the caves and went
deeper than we ever did before. Shit, this place is
freaky and gives us all the creeps, but at least we’re
safe here for now. I got through to the refuge at the
Godafoss falls, it seems only a couple of hundred
made it in there, but at least they are safe for now
too. I can only hope lots got off planet before the
last rad storm hit us.”1 0 .

N ESSA MAJ KEN
Confused, bitter and resentful, Majken has been a
Marauder for many years. However, she has decided
fighting against the Perfected is fruitless. She learned
much from devotee prisoners, and knows they seek
navigation data. This trip—with the help of her
sabotage and a downloaded copy of the Spirit of
Trafalgar’s nav data—was the perfect opportunity.
She needs to get to the Skritio Caves and give the
data to her new masters. The PCs can attempt an
opposed MANIPULATION test to see that she is hiding
something.

EVENTS
C L E A N U P C R E W S : The automated system at
Pelican Colony swiftly spots anything that is out of
place and sends D6 automatons to clean it up. That
includes the PCs, their vehicles and Solovetsky Island
itself. One Turn after the PCs stop in any location,
they will see these robots approaching. They will
immediately proceed to disassemble, salvage and take
away anything they can. It will take them one Shift to
salvage and remove a vehicle like a Daihotai tractor.
For the SEV, they will salvage one point of hull or
armor per Shift, completely salvaging a Magellan-class
in three days.
259G A M E
M O T H E R
S E C T I O N
R E S C U E T H E M A R A U D E R S : Whilst exploring
the city the PCs hear a shout for help and the toneless
voice of an automaton saying: “Please do not resist.”
The PCs see J.V. Gorham and Nessa Majken in the
grasp of two automatons. They have been captured
and are being returned to the Godafoss Caverns for
their own safety. When they see the PCs Gorham and
Majken fear they are devotees but will shout for help
as soon as they realize the PCs are not from the death
cult. If the PCs win Gorham’s trust she will suggest
they join forces, and Majken—the traitor—will be very
keen to have the PCs along if it further convinces
Gorham to explore the Skritio Caves.
F E A R T H E F I R E N A D O E S : A spark near the PCs
bursts into flame and, whipped up by the winds, imme-
diately swirls into a terrifying tornado of fire. It moves
at a rate of two zones per Round, in a random direction,
and burns everything it touches with an Intensity 12 fire.
Automated robots will appear within D6 Rounds to put
the fires out, but they will also be desperate to remove
the PCs from danger, by force if necessary.
B R I N G M E S U N S H I N E : The sun sends a Strong
radiation storm across KOI-947.01, causing 1 Rad per
Turn for characters in the open without protection.
The storm lasts 2D6 Turns. However, the storm is so
strong that even those protected by a ship, vehicle or
compression suit still suffer Weak radiation. The only
safe place is inside the Guardian ship. At your discre-
tion, to really turn up the heat, a storm could be so
strong that it brings Extreme radiation instead.
D I V I N E J OY : While on the Guardian ship Nessa
Majken cannot conceal her wonder and joy at the
majesty of the place. She is becoming increasingly
ecstatic that she has found the higher power she is
looking for. The PCs will notice this, but it’s up to them
if they think there may be a nefarious reason behind it.
T H E C H I L D R E N R E T U R N : At a point to best
heighten the tension, the Heliades-class ship that
Gorham had been chasing before the Spirit of Tra-
falgar crashed, reappears. Crewed by six devotees,
they will be searching for the survivors from the
crash and will detect the Solovetsky Island if the
ship is in the vicinity. They want to prevent the
survivors from escaping and capture the PCs’ ship
for themselves.
FINALE
T H E A B O M I N AT I O N H O R D E : After the
encounter with the Perfected, the PCs will have made
enough noise that the Abominations in the Spire have
awoken. The PCs suddenly hear echoing shrieks and
caterwauls from all over, no idea where they come
from—the Abominations are after them. This should
become a desperate chase to escape the Guardian,
not a stand-up fight. Have the PCs spot some Stage III
Revenants in the distance, and spring one on them as
a surprise. A Stage IV Beluga-Head and Stage V Sham-
bler block the corridor they have chosen to flee down.
Once outside, the PCs are safe from the Abominations,
as they are reluctant to brave the radiation.
T H E G U A R D I A N S H I P I S D E S T R OY E D : If the
Guardian ship is destroyed it implodes, bringing down
the mountainside and destroying the dam. Anyone (or
anything) on the plain by the dam and Hoppipolla lake
26 0
will have three Rounds to escape before being swept
away. If the UNCSS Solovetsky Island has landed here
a PILOT roll is needed to avoid the water, which does
three points of damage every Round the ship does not
escape. Those driving a vehicle must race away from
the water, making a PILOT roll each Round to keep
ahead—a failed roll and the vehicle is caught, and all
aboard take an eight Base Dice attack, Damage 1, for
each of the next three Rounds as they are swept up. If
they have swerved
the PILOT roll achieves three
into a safe spot, and the flood passes them by. Any
characters on foot will be swept away to their deaths.
If the PCs destroy the Guardian ship, by blowing up
or overloading the power conduits in the Power cham-
ber aboard the ship, the threat is destroyed, but if not,
the Perfected will eventually claim Pelican Colony for
themselves.1 0 .
E X P E D I T I O N S
EPILOGUE
There is little to recommend Pelican Colony for future
re-colonization, although some overzealous corporate
executive might sponsor a covert mission to acquire
any remains of the Engineer vessel. They may find
more than they bargained for, and return as an Abomi-
nation to the fleet. ■
METAPUZZLE CLUE #6—TRANSLATION OF THE ENGINEER HIEROGLYPH IN THE GUARDIAN SHIP

I N T H E S H A D O W
O F P E R F E C T I O N
“The gem cannot be polished without
friction, nor man Perfected without trials.”
—CHINESE PROVERB
This is the finale of The Lost Worlds campaign. Having
learned what they think is the truth, the PCs must rush
to the Lychgate to prevent the Perfected from using it.
They will battle to its heart before they understand it is
all a ruse, that the Perfected’s real prize is the UNCSS
Ìyánlá and all it carries. Avoiding the Xeno­morphs that
now infest the Lychgate, the PCs must join the battle
for Ìyánlá, a battle complicated by the UPP’s treachery
and own attempt to take control of the Great Mother
Mission. How the PCs resolve this conflict is up to
them, but the fate of humanity is in their hands.
261G A M E
M O T H E R
S E C T I O N
W H AT I S G O I N G O N ?
By now, the PCs will have learned what they think
is the truth—the Perfected are planning to use the
Engineer Lychgate, in orbit around the super gas giant
Ojo in the KOI-1938 system, to instantly travel the 100
light years between the Far Spinward Colonies and
the Middle Heavens. Their infection will spread, and
humanity will face its doom.
However, unknown to the PCs, the Perfected
cannot operate the Lychgate, and instead have made
another plan—to leak knowledge of the Lychgate to
the Great Mother Mission, knowing that in their ava-
rice, the humans won’t be able to resist seizing it for
themselves. In so doing, they will bring ships, perhaps
even the great colony ship UNCSS Ìyánlá, to within the
Perfected’s grasp. The Perfected will take these ships,
and in triumph journey to the Middle Heavens.
All they need to do is wait upon the Lychgate, with
their ships hiding in the near vicinity, holding their
fire until the right moment to spring the trap. Those
humans who venture on to the Engineer structure will
T H E T H R E E PA R T S
OF THE FINALE
PA R T I : The PCs arrive in the orbit of Ojo and find
the Lychgate. They should explore the Lychgate in
an attempt to prevent the Perfected from using it
as a portal, eventually confronting the Perfected
and Mother Ma’Kayla in the Lychgate’s Core. They
will learn the terrible truth behind the truth, that
this is all a honey pot, a trap to bring Ìyánlá within
the Perfected’s grasp, and that the battle for Ìyánlá
is about to begin.
PA R T I I : The PCs must escape the Lychgate and
the Xeno­morphs. They may be captured and read-
ied as hosts but will have the chance to escape.
PA R T I I I : The battle for Ìyánlá. Multiple factions
are trying to gain control of the ship and its vast
resources—the UPP have decided to take control,
the Perfected and the Children of the Two Divines
are trying to seize it, and the rest of the Mission’s
crew are trying to resist both of them. It’s up to the
PCs which, if any, of these factions they want to
support or oppose, and they should return to the
vessel to see out the fight, one way or another.
26 2
serve a useful function nonetheless, as the Lychgate
itself now has another purpose—the Perfected have
established four hives of XX121 Xeno­morphs aboard,
each with a growing Queen vying for the favor of the
one to rule them all, the Empress.
Gaius aboard the Ìyánlá is made aware of the Lych-
gate, either by the PCs contacting him and briefing him
themselves, or the Solovetsky Island’s DA/UT/UR com-
puter will have sent the information to him via Ìyánlá’s
MU/TH/UR. The fleet sets sail for the KOI-1938 system.
As the Ìyánlá drops from FTL and heads for the
orbit of Ojo, the UPP launches its coup to take control
of the Great Mother Mission. They resuscitate their
covert soldiers from hypersleep and ready themselves
to take over. But not all the UPP are focused on this
treachery. Unknown to the PCs, a UPP Cosmos Explo-
ration Corps scout ship under Lt Col Sensakovic has
already arrived at the Lychgate—she knows the threat
the Perfected represent and is already aboard the
Lychgate with the same mission as the PCs.
WHAT’S THE STORY, MOTHER?
You set sail for the KOI-1938 system in search of the
Lychgate, with the Ìyánlá and the fleet just hours
behind you in support. You find the gas giant, Ojo, a
planet that makes Jupiter look like a pebble in com-
parison. And there before you, orbiting this wonder of
nature, lies another wonder—the Lychgate.
You had thought Ìyánlá was impressive, but this
structure is truly awe-inspiring. Not quite circular, kilo-
meters across, with an immense outer ring connected
to a central hub by 16 spiraling booms, interlaced with
smaller girders that twist and writhe between the
spokes. The outer ring has four great transepts, huge
hangers hundreds of meters across and open to space,
easily big enough to swallow your ship and still have
space for more. The central hub, a massive flattened
sphere seemingly fashioned by the hands of the gods
themselves, is itself over one thousand meters across
and three hundred meters thick.
Your ship sensors show faint traces of power
running throughout the majestic structure. Spikes
of intensity and temperature increase as you scan
towards the central core, the beating heart of the gate.
The thermal signature blooms mightily at the very
center of the leviathan construction.
The Lychgate spins in breathtakingly elegant laziness,
a timeless behemoth that neither fears nor remembers
the passing of the eons. It turns, bathed in the radiant
glow from the yellow super gas giant, and waits.1 0 .
KICKING OFF
THE ACTION
The action kicks off in space near the Lychgate.
The PCs can see two Heliades-class ships, the
Perfected with their devotee minions from the
Children of the Two Divines, maneuvering into
position, easing themselves into two of the four
Transepts, preparing to dock and board the Lych-
gate. They have an hour’s head start (10 Turns).
Piloting Solovetsky Island into a Transept and
parking it close to the Airlock Spheres requires a
PILOTING roll with a −1 modification. A failed roll
means they have scraped the ship or struggled
with the Lychgate’s rotation—they successfully
complete the maneuver, but the ship takes
D3 damage.
“If you don’t stop it there won’t be
a home to go back to. It’s carrying
death and heading for Earth.”
— D R E L I Z A B E T H S H AW
THE LYCHGATE’S
ENVIRONMENT
With the exception of the Outer Ring, which is open
to the vacuum of space, the Lychgate is pressur-
ized and has a breathable, if humid, atmosphere.
Residual power flows and creates a low blue glow
throughout, that seems to emanate from everywhere
but nowhere at the same time. The solid core is
intensely dense, and has an exotic gravitational
effect, while the entire structure is spinning on its
axis. This means that the gravity felt in the center,
on the surface of the core itself, is much stronger
than that felt at the outer surface. While the gravi-
tational effect is obviously gradual, in game terms
the Core is 1.5G, the Antechamber Tunnels are 1G,
the Booms and Ambulatories are 0.5G, and it’s zero
G in the Outer Ring. The PCs will suffer from gravity
dyspraxia (page 91) as they travel through the
different zones.

THE FINALE’S GUEST STARS
Many of the NPCs from the campaign may feature in
this expedition, assuming they survive to this point
in the story. You can incorporate them in the scenario
as you see fit—some are aboard the Lychgate, others
on the Ìyánlá
Ìyánlá,, and the rest can appear when you need
them to. The key ones are:

from the expeditions Against a Sea Of Troubles and
Let Sleeping Gods Lie survive, they will be aboard
the Lychgate or leading the Perfected’s attack on
the Ìyánlá
Ìyánlá..

the PCs when they reach the Lychgate’s Core.
GENERAL NURLAN OZOLINSKI (PAGE 150): He is
leading the UPP’s attempts to take control of UNCSS
Ìyánlá. He is a reasonable man, and if the PCs can
Ìyánlá.
convince him of the threat posed by the Perfected
and their minions, he will order his troops to fight
them, instead of taking over the ship.
ALECTO THROOP (PAGE 170): She and her rescue
ships are not combat troops, but she wants to help in
the fight against the UPP takeover and the Perfected.
She will use her ships to transport the PCs, or to
rescue them from a tight spot, should they need it.
J.V. GORHAM (PAGE 145): The purpose of her life,
and that of her ancestors, has been to oppose the
Perfected. She and the Gorham’s Marauders may
arrive to join the final battle against the Perfected,
with four ships and 50 fighters.
WARLORD ZHĀNGJIÉ AND/OR BRIGADIER WŎ (PAGE
145 AND 223): While the Cooperative is a self-in-
terested society that thinks it can defend itself, the
PCs can try to persuade Zhāngjié and/or Wŏ that
helping against the Perfected is in their best inter-
ests. The Cooperative may arrive to help, with two
ships and 50 soldiers, but may turn traitor and side
with the UPP, depending on their relationship with
the PCs.
LIEUTENANT COLONEL VICTOR DRUBOV (PAGE 231):
If Drubov survived he and his men are recalled to
UNCSS Ìyánlá to support the UPP takeover. However,
depending on his relationship with the PCs he may
support them in their moment of need.
263G A M E
M O T H E R
S E C T I O N
T H E LY C H G A T E
The Lychgate is unmistakably an enormous Engineer
relic, its seemingly symmetrical structure twisted with
bulges, curves and swirls that give its biomechanical
design an almost organic feel. Seeing it for the first
time brings +1 STRESS LEVEL.
THE OUTER RING
This entire ring is hollow and open to the vacuum of
space—a huge Engineer ship hangar bay. While the
height of this ring varies between 500 and 150 meters
it is uniformly 800 meters wide. The interior walls are
curved and shaped to allow Juggernauts and other
vessels of unknown design to dock, hugging them-
selves snugly into the shaped docking spaces made for
them. On the outer hull there are similar slots where
a Guardian ship could attach, although the Lychgate
hasn’t played host to an Engineer vessel in millennia.
T R A N S E P T S : Huge openings that allow ships to
maneuver into the interior of the Outer Ring. Two of
them house Perfected Heliades-class ships.
A I R L O C K S P H E R E S : Where each Ambulatory con-
nects with the Outer Ring there are six airlock spheres,
each 50 meters across and fashioned in organic shapes
and lines. Each airlock has a 10-meter circular open-
ing on one side, the entrance and exit aperture, that
allows access to the interior of the sphere, but cannot
be docked with—the PCs must spacewalk to gain
access to the airlock. Inside it’s full of outcrops and
girders—ribbed platforms to stand or hold on to. Once
someone enters the sphere, the ancient automated
mechanisms take over, swiveling the entire sphere 180
degrees. The aperture swings round and slowly reveals
the view on the other side. When the aperture turns
from the vacuum of the Outer Ring to the atmosphere
of the Ambulatory, the sphere is suddenly flooded by a
rush of air. When turning from atmosphere to vacuum,
the air in the sphere explosively decompresses—unless
the PCs have prepared for this (by taking hold of the
platforms or attaching a cable to secure themselves),
they must make a MOBILITY test or be whooshed into
the zero-G vacuum of the Outer Ring.
THE BOOM SPOKES
A M B U L AT O R I E S : Accessed from the Outer Ring
through the Airlock Spheres, the Ambulatories are
huge twisted, spiraling tunnels, 100 meters wide. The
spirals make multiple pathways that twist around
the edges, allowing the PCs to make their way down
the tunnel. At the base of the tunnel, the PCs see ten
hatches set in the floor, five meters wide and made of
the same organically shaped substance of the airlock
spheres. Several are open, either fully or just enough
for a human to squeeze through. The Ambulatory has
a cathedral-like feel—sounds echo, the air swirls with
dust, and the glowing blue haze makes light beams
dance in the shadows.
26 4
B O O M L AT T I C E S : What look like structural girders
from the outside, are actually two-meter-wide tunnels
that create a warren of paths between the Ambula-
tories. Each Ambulatory has dozens of openings to
these twisting, dark and cold pipes. A source of light
is needed to navigate them, and once inside, the PCs
need to make an OBSERVATION roll to avoid getting
lost within the maze. They can make this roll once per
Turn but gain +1 STRESS LEVEL on the first failed roll,
and must make a Panic Roll if they fail a second time.
They gain a +1 modification if they use a Pups to aid
them (page 93).1 0 .

THE ANTECHAMBER TUNNELS
Entering this space from an Ambulatory the PCs see
a bewildering maze of multiple tunnels crisscrossing
each other, all heading down.
As the PCs negotiate these tunnels they will come
across a number of random chambers—rolled on the
adjacent table—before they eventually either reach
an iris-valve hatch in the floor that opens, leading to
the Lychgate Core (if they are heading downwards),
or the hatches to the Ambulatory (if they are trying
to leave):
D6CHAMBER TABLE
1A cryosleep room with D66 beds lined up vertically around the walls, all empty.
2A wide chamber with an obsidian plinth in the middle, watched over by four carved heads.
3If the PCs are exploring the Lychgate, this is an empty chamber. If they are fleeing the Xeno­morphs
after the confrontation at the Core, it is a Xeno­morph hive chamber with D6 Facehuggers, D6 Ovo-
morphs, and D6 hosts. If the PCs linger a Drone will appear, at your discretion.
4A room with small pools of crystal-clear water, and drapes hanging throughout. The PCs have to
push through them to progress.
5The centerpiece of the chamber is a three-meter-wide shaft, dripping water and full of dusty mist.
Roll D6. On 1–3, it’s on the ceiling and goes upwards, on 4–6, it’s on the floor and goes down.
6A shrine of some sort with images and glyphs lining the walls, but too eroded to make any sense of.
T H E LY C H G A T E C O R E
The core chamber is a 300-meter-wide sphere, with
dozens of iris-valve hatches scattered around the
ceiling. There are no obvious controls, but they
open when touched. In the center of the chamber
is the Core, a huge sphere that forms a surface, 100
meters below the ceiling and its hatches. The space
in between is crisscrossed by an intricate scaffold of
twisted girders, pipes and small platforms.
S C A F F O L D : Built for humanoids bigger than
humans, the scaffold forms a set of stairs and walk-
ways for the Engineers to reach the surface from the
hatches. For the PCs, it requires a MOBILITY roll to
clamber up or down. A failed roll means they slip and
crash into a nearby girder, taking one point of damage
(armor applies).
S U R FA C E A N D S U N K E N T R E N C H E S : Standing
on the surface of the Core, underneath the spider’s
web of scaffolding, under 1.5G of gravity, is an intensely
weird experience. Being only 200 meters across the
266
ground of the core appears to fall away from the PCs
on all sides. Gain +1 STRESS LEVEL. The surface is criss-
crossed by narrow trenches, all linked and converging
on a hexagonal cynosure, the center of the Lychgate.
C Y N O S U R E : Sunken into the surface, the Cynosure
is the Lychgate’s control center. A central chair, high-
backed and looming, and surrounded by musical con-
trols, sits between four space jockey platforms, each
facing the chair. The PCs will not be able to activate
any of the musical controls even if they sit in the chair.
But if one should climb into a space jockey seat, the
suit will automatically start to close over them. Unless
they immediately make a successful MOBILITY roll they
are trapped inside, the suit giving them Armor Rating

THE FIGHT FOR THE CYNOSURE
When the PCs arrive at the Cynosure, they find a calm
scene: a Perfected (one they have already met, if they sur-
vived), Mother Ma’Kayla and six devotees are waiting for
them. They won’t start any hostilities, knowing full well
that the Xeno­morphs are gathering in the scaffold and
looking for hosts, but will defend themselves if attacked.
The PCs are swamped with telepathic images of
welcome, of a joyful reunion, of hope, shrouded within
a cloak of an iron willpower and utter ruthlessness.
Mother Ma’Kayla will then greet them in a non-aggres-
sive way, and say the following:
TShe openly admits she cannot make the machine
work but says “feel free to try it for yourselves.”
TShe will tell them that the Perfected have been here
for months, and have always known they couldn’t
operate it, “but making it work wasn’t the point—
bringing you and your ships here was…”
TShe will try to convince them to join the Perfected:
“Why bother fighting us, when you can join us and
reap the joys of perfection?”
TIf the PCs refuse her offer, she will seem genuinely
disappointed, but will shrug her shoulders: “It mat-
ters little, by now our people will be on their way to
capture your Ìyánlá and we will soon be on our way
to the Middle Heavens.”
During this scene—or as the fight unfolds, if the PCs
choose to attack—the Xeno­morphs’ presence in the
scaffolding becomes more obvious. The PCs can make
an opposed OBSERVATION roll to hear or spot move-
ment in the scaffold, before two Xeno­morphs sweep
down and take two of her devotees. Two Scouts and
two Drones now close in on the PCs, intent on captur-
ing them (use the Xeno­morph Capture Attacks below).
Draw initiative.
THE XENOMORPHS AND THE HIVES
The XX121 Xeno­morphs aboard the Lychgate behave a little differently from those in the core rulebook. Four hives
are being cultivated, under the overall control of an Empress, and there is competition between the hives. These
Xeno­morphs are in “capture mode” with the gathering of live hosts for the hives their primary instinct. This overrides
individual self-preservation, the scouts and drones are driven to capture hosts even if they are attacked themselves.
XENOMORPH CAPTURE ATTACKS
D6ATTACK
1HERDING: The Xeno­morph spreads its limbs, bares its teeth and shepherds the victim. The victim must win
an opposed MOBILITY roll against ten Base Dice or be forced to move wherever the Xeno­morph wants—near
a Facehugger, into the arms of another Drone or Scout, or somewhere else where capturing the PC is made
easier. Make an immediate Panic Roll.
2
NO ESCAPE: The Xeno­morph pauses and hisses at its victim, before scampering away to an adjacent zone. But
the Xeno­morph is only biding its time—when it acts on the next Round, it has been joined by another of the
same type, and they both attack the original target.
3
BRING THEM DOWN: The Xeno­morph sweeps with arms, legs and tail, lashing out to bring the victim to the
ground. It attacks with ten Base Dice against the target’s CLOSE COMBAT. If successful, the target is battered to
the ground, drops any handheld items, suffers one point of damage and must make an immediate Panic Roll.
4
FACE GRAB: The Xeno­morph grasps the victim’s face, an opposed grappling attack with eight Base Dice. If the
Xeno­morph succeeds, it does no damage, but the victim is grappled, blinded, and must make an immediate
Panic Roll. If the victim does not break the grapple, the Xeno­morph’s next attack is automatically #6.
5
CAPTURE FOR THE HIVE: The Xeno­morph attacks with its venom-spiked tail, with ten Base Dice, Damage 1.
If the attack causes any damage, the Xeno­morph pulls its punch so only one point of damage is inflicted,
and the paralyzing venom takes effect. The victim must make a STAMINA roll—the number of
rolled is the
number of Rounds they can stay up, then they fall unconscious for D6 Turns. The paralysis can be removed
with a shot of adrenaline (a MEDICAL AID roll with a medkit).
6
STUN THE HOST: The Xeno­morph attacks the victim with nine Base Dice, Damage 1, its inner jaw flashing out. But
it’s not trying to kill. If the attack does any damage, the victim is immediately Broken and knocked unconscious
by the blow. They do not suffer any critical effect even though they are Broken, but are unconscious for D6 Turns.

LIEUTENANT CO LO N EL SO NIA S EN SAKOVIC
the UPP’s desire to ensure the Great Mother Mission
is a success for the people of the UPP but has misgiv-
ings about the military approach. She has seen the
Perfected firsthand and knows the threat they present.
She has come to stop the Perfected using the Lych-

If the PCs save her and help her escape the Lych-

C O M M A N D M O D U L E : Houses the Bridge (which
includes control of Ìyánlá’s complement of nuclear
weapons), Communications Center and the UN Mis-
sion Administration offices.
T R A N S I T M O D U L E : The primary module for per-
sonnel access to and from Ìyánlá. It contains airlock
access from the SEV docking ring, hangar bays and
tactical operations centers, for coordinating off-ship
operations, and the security ops room, with armory.
This only contains some small arms weapons (pistols
and rifles) at your discretion.
C R YO S L E E P M O D U L E S A – D : Each module
contains 2,500 sleeping colonists.
E N G I N E E R I N G : Maintenance and control of ship
systems are managed from here (with the exception
of drive control) as well as bulk hangers for on and
off-loading cargo. UNCSS Ìyánlá’s security CCTV and
environment systems can be controlled from the Engi-
neering Control room at the aft of this module, includ-
ing atmosphere and power. This module also serves as
bulk storage for everything the mission needs, from
food and water, rescue supplies and spare parts, to
mining equipment, explosive charges, Powerloaders
and anything else an enterprising PC might think of
(at your discretion).
270
The PCs could influence the outcome of the battle
by occupying the Engineering Control room and
remotely tampering with Ìyánlá’s systems using COM-
TECH —see the sidebar Running Interference.
T H E T H R E E S P I N E S : Three structural corridors
that run the length of the ship, one central spine for
bulk equipment, and starboard and port spines for
crew. Each has a travelator both fore and aft direc-
tions, and safety bulkheads every 50 meters.
D R I V E M O D U L E : Everything needed to propel the
ship. The reactor complex is a suite of five rooms that
surround and support the ship’s reactors. Emergency
self-destruct controls are located here, but can only
be authorized by UNCSS Ìyánlá’s senior flight officer
and Governor Abantu.
Without their authorization codes the system can
be hacked, but it is hard, requiring a COMTECH roll
with a −3 modification, and a Turn of work, during
which tamper alarms will sound throughout the ship.
After that, the ship will self-destruct two Turns later.
The Drive Module also houses the compressed fuel
store. An explosive charge placed against a critical
spot (requiring a HEAVY MACHINERY roll to identify)
will breach the tanks and set off a chain reaction
that will cause a welter of explosions to destroy the
ship in 3D6 Rounds. The same effect can be gained
by piloting an SEV into the Drive Module at the right
place, requiring a HEAVY MACHINERY roll to locate the
weak spot in the module’s structure, and a PILOTING
roll to hit it.1 0 .
RUNNING INTERFERENCE
If the PCs occupy the Engineering Control room, they
can use the systems there to affect the Ìyánlá’s envi-
ronment. Using COMTECH , the PCs can access the CCTV
system to find friends and enemies aboard the ship, or
survey the situation in critical locations, such as the
bridge or drive rooms. They can track the movement of
enemy forces and feed information to friendly troops.
E X P E D I T I O N S
COMTECH will enable them to open and close bulkheads
and airlocks, depressurize areas, and hold the enemy to
ransom. The opportunities are only limited by the PCs’
imaginations, and your discretion. Once the PCs start
doing this, they are likely to draw unwanted attention
from their enemies, who will attack engineering to put
a stop to them.
EVENTS
S O U N D S I N T H E D A R K : While aboard the Lych-
gate the PCs hear hissing from the darkness, and a
bank of steamy fog rolls towards them from a nearby
tunnel. With a successful OBSERVATION roll, they can
hear what sounds like scraping footfalls from within
the mist—and gain +1 STRESS LEVEL —and their visi-
bility is immediately reduced to SHORT range for one
Turn. At your discretion the steam can hide a Facehug-
ger on the prowl (page 302 of the core rulebook).
T H E D E A D U P P : As the PCs explore the Lychgate,
they stumble across the dead body of a soldier in
UPP 6B90 armor, his chest such a mangled mess
it’s impossible to tell exactly what killed him. If the
PCs search the body they find a name tag, Sergeant
Maksim Yurelko, an MP-4043 pistol with 2 reloads, and
a combat knife. Sgt Yurelko was one of UPP Lt Colonel
Sensakovic’s missing soldiers.
S N A K E S K I N : As the PCs explore the Lychgate and
get closer to the Core they find sticky piles of what
look like sloughed-off snake skin. They vary in size, but
some are almost the size of a human. This may bring
+1 STRESS LEVEL to all seeing it, at your discretion.
T H E E N E M Y O F M Y E N E M Y : While exploring
the Lychgate, the PCs stumble across Lt Colonel Sen-
sakovic, one UPP soldier and her AA83 Davydovich
combat android (page 171). She has lost contact
with the rest of her team, although one has remained
on her scout ship docked in the Outer Ring. She is wary
but may divulge that she is there to stop the Lychgate
being used and can be persuaded to join forces.
O H N O YO U D O N ’ T : Once the PCs learn of the
Perfected’s plan and are attempting to flee the Lych-
gate, Xeno­morphs set off to recapture them. Two
Drones are scurrying along tunnels to get ahead. Enter
stealth mode. Feel free to adjust the number of Xeno­
morphs where that will help build the tension of the
chase, and to use the original Signature Attack tables
(page 309 of the core rulebook).
T H I S O N E I S M I N E : When a PC is about to be
killed or captured by a Xeno­morph, another Xeno­
morph attacks, but it doesn’t attack the PC. The two
beasts, from competing hives, square off against one
another in a display of intimidating ferocity intended
to make the weaker creature back down. The PC gains
+1 STRESS LEVEL , but it’s their chance to run like hell.
T H E C H I L D R E N F I N D YO U : While trying to
leave the Lychgate and escape being captured as
Xeno­morph hosts, the PCs run into a group of three
devotees who will block their escape. They will say the
PCs are honored to have been chosen by the Destroy-
ing Angels and shouldn’t insult them by resisting. They
will fight to restrain the PCs and return them to the
Xeno­morphs. At your discretion, a Xeno­morph may
appear, but take a devotee first!

M O T H E R
S E C T I O N
I T ’ S W E I R D A N D P I S S E D O F F : While escaping from
the Lychgate the PCs take a turn and run into a big, hot
and humid chamber—definitely a hive. In the center is the
Empress Xeno­morph, blocking the PCs’ path. +1 STRESS
LEVEL and immediate Panic Rolls for all who see this. She
will make a PSYCHIC LOVE attack every Round against a
random PC (Empress Signature Attack #2, page 138), until
this fails, in which case she will MIND MELT (Attack #6) the
PC who resisted. Probably time for the PCs to run like hell
the other way.
THE BATTLE FOR ÌYÁNLÁ
The battle for Ìyánlá can play out in many
different ways, depending on the actions
of the PCs and what you feel builds the
greatest tension for this finale. Options
include:
TThe Perfected get the upper hand and
look like they will attain victory, and
possession of the Ìyánlá
Ìyánlá,, quickly. This
could be indicated by UPP forces falling
back from key positions, the destruction
of a friendly ship, or Governor Abantu
giving the order to abandon ship.
H AV O C A B O A R D Ì YÁ N L Á : Xeno­morph Drones have
been released on UNCSS Ìyánlá by the Perfected. The PCs
hear the effects of their violence over the radio and come
face to face with a Xeno­morph of your choice at a critical
moment in the action.
TThe UPP gets the upper hand, indicated
P R AY F O R T H E C AVA L R Y : If the battle for Ìyánlá
needs spicing up, or the PCs need some extra help, or they
have arranged for help, the cavalry finally arrives. It might
be Gorham’s Marauders, or the Cooperative, throwing their
troops into the fight, or UPP Colonels Drubov or Sensa-
kovic turn up at the right moment. Remember you have
these tools to help direct the battle into the most tense and
exciting finale you can.
by the destruction of a Perfected ship,
the capture of key locations such as the
Bridge or Drive Module, or Governor
Abantu orders the surrender to the UPP,
to save lives.
TThe battle is a close run thing, with no
one getting the upper hand as soldiers
fight, the ship gets increasingly dam-
aged, and people die.
THE FINALE
The epic finale of The Lost Worlds campaign plays
out on and around the home of the Great Mother
Mission itself, the UNCSS Ìyánlá. In space there will
be numerous small ships from Ìyánlá, including the
UNCSS Umsindisi and UNCSS Chimata-no-kami. There
are four Heliades-class vessels from the Children of
the Two Divines, docked or trying to dock with Ìyánlá,
boarding their attackers to take the ship.
C O M M S C H AT T E R : The radio waves are full of
comms chatter as a result of the fighting—the PCs
can learn what is happening by hacking into these
comms with a successful COMTECH roll from aboard
the Solovetsky Island, or a suitable console aboard the
Ìyánlá, or using a Seegson P-DAT (page 132 of the core
rulebook). You can add whatever information you feel
the PCs need to make this final battle as exciting as
possible.
T H R E E W O R L D E M P I R E : Colonel David Buston
and Lynna Young-Hee put aside their differences
272
and join the UNISC security forces fighting the UPP’s
attempted coup.
U N I T E D A M E R I C A S : Valentina Berezi and the UA
contingent aboard the Ìyánlá are glad the gloves are
off and it’s not the UA’s fault—they resist the UPP with
everything they have.
W E Y L A N D -Y U TA N I : Kamal Vartouhi, in best
Weyland-Yutani style, secretly negotiates with General
Ozolinski to make sure the company comes out of this
shit-show smelling of roses, however the battle turns
out. Gaius, however, remains neutral and keeps the
Great Mother Mission’s best interests at heart.
T H E O T H E R C O R P O R AT E I N T E R E S T S : Hyper-
dyne, Omni-Tech Resources and Kelland Mining realize
they are in over their heads and want nothing to do
with the fighting. They all work to swipe whatever
valuable discoveries are in the Ìyánlá’s science labs
and quarantine bays and get off the ship.1 0 .
DEFENDING THE ÌYÁNLÁ
The battle for the ship will play out in many locations.
The table below explains what the UPP forces, and the
Perfected and their devotees, are trying to achieve
at the point the PCs enter the action. You as GM will
need to decide, and narrate, the action in some areas
to further the excitement of this final confrontation.
This should be driven by the actions of the PCs and the
E X P E D I T I O N S
plans they come up with—throw extra challenges in
their way or remove a challenge that stands in the way
of a great idea. For example, if the PCs want to go to
the Reactor Room, they will have little chance against
all the enemy forces listed there, so narrate the battle
that sees the opposing forces destroy each other and
gives the PCs a fighting chance.

B AT T L E D A M A G E : To reflect the damage the ship
is taking from the battle, roll on the Minor Component
Damage table (page 198 of the core rulebook) once
per Turn after the battle starts. There should be three
rolls before the PCs even reach the ship. Narrate these
results into the ongoing story of the battle for the Ìyánlá.
D E S T R OY I N G T H E Ì YÁ N L Á : The PCs may
decide the only way to stop the Perfected winning is
to destroy the Ìyánlá. There are several ways they can
achieve this:
Set the self-destruct sequence using the controls
in the Drive Module. This takes one Turn and will
destroy the ship two Turns after that.
Set an explosive charge to destroy the compressed
fuel store in the Drive Module. This will destroy the
ship in 3D6 Rounds.

which will destroy the ship in 3D6 Rounds.

module which will cause the ship to break up in 3D6
Turns and be fully destroyed in 3D6 Shifts.
Take control of the Ìyánlá’s bridge and either det-
onate one of the ship’s store of nukes, or crash the
colony ship into the crushing depths of Ojo.
I C A N ’ T L E T YO U D O T H AT : Two Working Joe
androids (page 172) will see that the PCs are attempt-
ing to self-destruct the Ìyánlá or blow up the fuel tanks
or intend to crash the Solovetsky Island into the colony
ship. They approach saying: “This activity is highly
dangerous, for your own safety I cannot allow you to
continue,” and will use non-lethal force to restrain the
PCs and stop them completing their task. ■
273G A M E
M O T H E R
S E C T I O N
A F T E R M A T H
The aftermath depends on the outcome of the Battle
of the Ìyánlá.
The worst, for humanity’s sake, is the Perfected
win. They take their contagion on their captured ships
and head for the Middle Heavens. The survivors from
the Battle of the Ìyánlá have a choice. They can flee
into the Far Spinward Colonies with whatever strength
they can muster, and start life over, but with the Sword
of Damocles hanging over their head—waiting for the
day when the Perfected, or the Xeno­morphs, or the
Engineers return to wipe them out. Or they can race
home, to call upon the fighting forces of the 3WE, the
UPP and the USCMC to put aside their differences, to
stand and confront this threat, starting a new story—
a new campaign—as humanity fights back.
However, the Battle of the Ìyánlá may not be so cut
and dried—a victory for humanity but the dregs of the
Perfected remain. Ìyánlá is infected so severely by the
Perfected it cannot be recovered. The survivors rush
to evacuate all they can from the great ship, before
plunging it into the heart of a nearby sun and finding
somewhere to settle. The old and established colonies
would surely welcome them, or new colonies just
274
starting up that could use their skills. But the Per-
fected are still a threat, and there are many stories to
be told of hunting them down and incinerating every
last scrap of infection.
And the best—the Perfected are annihilated, their
ships destroyed and the Children of the Two Divines
dead or scattered. There are still worlds to scour clean
but without ships the ragged Perfected that remain
are impotent. The survivors can look to their future,
complete the survey of the Far Spinward Colonies, and
set up home, perhaps on a pristine world, untouched
by either human or Perfected hands, and start a whole
new story of exploration and colonization.
But the Lychgate still remains, enigmatic and with
its deadly cargo. Weyland-Yutani won’t be letting this
go, and neither will the other corporations wanting
their cut. The United Nations, under the authority of
Governor Abantu, places a quarantine around it, but
how secure can that be? But for now, as everyone
licks their wounds and collects their wits, it holds. And
the Empress and her children, with timeless patience,
grow into their new empire, and wait. ■
